O sons, if I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, through its completion in it, and through its expositions and declarations, from my point of view, you will complete that to you with this treatise, which is the part of the operation by hand, and that is surgery.
Because the operation by hand is neglected in our region and in our time it is deprived of all, while greatly risking the science of it, and its practices are obscured; and nothing remains of it except a few small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which they distorted and led to errors, and confused the senses of it, and elongated its force and art.
And it is clear to me that you will enliven that through the ordering of this treatise according to the second way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and so that it may come with the forms of the tools of cautery and of other instruments of the work as it should be for addition through declaration, and for preparation of it, which cause is necessary.
But the cause why no good artificer is approved by his hand in our time, is because the art of medicine is long, and that its agent must first be exercised in the science of anatomy which recognizes the parts of members and their forms, and their conjunction and separation; and have the knowledge of bones, nerves, and vessels, and the number of these, and their issue; and of the pulsating veins and of the quiet ones, and the places of their issuing.
And for that Hyporcas says that although his name is great, in practice it is small, and especially in the art of the hand.
But we have already said of that in the introduction to this book; because whoever is not learned in what we have said of anatomy, is not evacuated so as not to fall into error through which men will die, just as I have seen many of those, because some are formed in this science and they throw themselves away from it without knowledge or experience.
Because I saw a foolish and experienced doctor who made an incision on a goiter on the neck of a woman, and he cut some arteries in the neck so that much blood flowed and the woman died in his hands.
And I saw another doctor who took a stone from a man's gallbladder, and the stone was large, and he took it out with a piece of the bladder, and that man died on the third day.
And I called to him to stop that, and I saw that through the size of the stone and the disposition of the patient over him that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who received wages from a duke of our land for surgery, and he cured a black slave whose leg was fractured; and through the ignorance of the doctor, he removed the fracture over the wound with powders and splints with strong compression, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
And he bound it according to his desires, and he relined it, and he left it for several days, and he commanded that we should not loose the bandage; and so it was as the leg and the thigh became infected with an ulcer, and it came to ruin.
And I was called to him, and I prepared to loose the bandage, and I found rest and ease of his pains.
But nevertheless corruption was confirmed in the member, so that I could not restrain it, and the corruption did not cease to wander through the member until the patient died.
And I saw another doctor who perforated a cancerous ulcer, and it was open for some days, so that the evil of it increased through its lord.
The cause of which is that the rotten ulcer is pure of melancholic humour, then it does not reach him by iron or anything else, but that it be in a member that suffers so as to be hostile to it.
And for that, sons, it is necessary for you that the operation by hand be divided into two divisions: one is an operation associated with health, and the other is work through which there is peril in the major dispositions.
And I have already discussed that in every place of this book where there is an operation in which there is error and fear; so it is necessary for you to guard against that and leave it, so that the foolish do not stop speaking and disgracing you.
And thus take your arms with diligence and the protection of God; and your patients with facility and firmness.
And use the better way through the grace of God so that you may attain health and praiseworthy succession, and lay waste to terrible illnesses of difficult cure; and hold your arms from what makes you fearful, so that trepidation in your faith and name may not escape you: for it remains for your glory, and more beyond in the world and in heaven for your sanctities.
Galia already said in some of his proverbs: “Do not heal illnesses ill, so that evil doctors are not named.”
And I have divided this book according to three titles.
Begin the division of the book, and first of the first part. The first chapter ordered from the head to the feet, in the forms of instruments and tools of cauteries, and what is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, of cautery and piercing, and of leeches, and of plasters, and of extraction of arrows and of similar things, all titled and ordered in the forms of instruments.
The third chapter, of restoration and of dislocation, and of cure of tortion and of similar things; a chapter ordered from the head to the feet, and of the forms of instruments.
I will tell you the quality of those cauteries and of their properties, and in what disposition cautery is prohibited.
Therefore I say that the word of the quality of cautery and the property of it is long and prolix, and subtle through science, and secret hid; and many wise men have spoken much of it, and they disagree on it, and for me enough is a little of their words, fearing prolixity.
And therefore I say that cautery confers upon every complete disposition universally the which is of matter or without matter, excepting two dispositions, which are caustic dispositions without matter.
In the caustic and dry disposition with matter disagreement; for some say that cautery is beneficial to it, and others the contrary of that, that cautery is not convenient in illness which is by quality and dryness, because the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and convening is that illness caustic and dry is cured by what is cauted and dry.
And he says the contrary of that, that by cautery there is benefit in every illness caustic and dry which one sees in the bodies of men, because when you compare the body of man and his humours to the disposition of fire, you find the body of man rubbed.
And I say by the word of that, that experiment it already to me several times have discovered.
But it is not appropriate to come upon this topic one who is inexperienced and un practiced in the chapter of cauteries through posterior exercise, and has not known the diversity of the complexions of men and the disposition of illnesses in their bodies, and their causes, and their accidents, and the span of time of those.
But in other complexions, do not fear; and especially in moist illnesses, for all doctors have agreed on those, and have not disagreed on the use of cauteries on them.
And know, sons, that the secret of cure by cautery with fire and its goodness, is because fire is simple, whose action does not reach except to the member which is cauterized, and does not affect another member with it except with little harm.
But the action of burning medicine reaches to those in members from which it is distant, and strongly brings the illness into the member with difficult cure, and strongly increases it.
But fire, by its sublimity and the goodness of its substance, does not do that except to cause superfluousness. And it is known to us through experience and through the length of service of study on the truth of causes; and because of this I am excused from the length of speech. And if it were not that I am not read in your presence in this pauserer, a secret hid by fire, and the quality of the operation of it in bodies and of its expulsion through which you expel illnesses, by philosophical speech demonstrated, which would be acute in your feet.
And know, sons, that they disagree on the time when it is convenient to do cautery and pause the best time of spring.
And I say that cautery is convenient in all times, so that the damage by the accidental time is submerged in the improvement of what is drawn by cautery, and especially if the cautery is for pains or necessary pains, strong and fiery, which do not endure delay because it is feared of those who come to wickedness, which is greater than little harm coming by time.
And thus do not cut into your feet, or sons, that which is not considered except by the common people and foolish doctors; it is because to that illness which is healed by cautery there is not a reduction of all time, and they pause that consequence.
And the cause is not because they think it; for cautery is only in place of medicine which alters the complexion and dries up the moisture, which are caused so that pains come.
But cautery is superfluous over medicine by the will of its strength and power, and greatness of his lordship.
And it is possible that his illness returns at some time of the year, according to the complexion of the patient and the location of his illness, and its strength, and that which is prepared in his body from the accumulation of superfluities in him, and that which has come to him in his acquisition in foods and likenesses of those causes; but that the illness on which cautery was administered is subtle illness in a member of few superfluities and moisture, thus like cautery of a tooth for pain and likeness, it is possible that this pain does not return in him, but that is done in small ones.
And yet the vulgar speech is that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, and it is a right speech, not so that they understand it in it, for they believe there is no cure which profits by medicine or other cause except cautery.
And the cause is in contrary to that; and the intention that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is only when we administer the methods of cure in certain illnesses, and those medicines do not confer it, and yet at the end of the cause a man is administered cautery, and profits from it. And then from here cut that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, not according to the intention which the vulgar and foolish doctors understand it.
And they said the ancients that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say it except for the equality of gold and sublimity of its substance.
And they said that the place of cautery does not do heat, when it is not absolutely true; for I have seen and proved that it does only in some bodies without the others, and cautery with that is good and better than with iron as they said; but when you do cautery with fire with gold, it is not declared to you, because it is heated according to the quantity that you will by the redness of the gold, and prepares to receive heat; and if you apply over it ignition, the gold melts into the fire, and drops some sheets so that the artificer cuts off by the occupation of that.
And therefore cautery is done with iron we must lightly and more closely to rectitude of operation.
And I have already ordered this chapter on cautery according to chapters, and have ordered those of the head within the feet, so that they ask from him what he wants of it.
The first chapter:
This cautery confers with moisture and coldness about the superficial accident of which it is two causes, so is cause of soda and multitude of fluxes, called corissa, from the parts of the ears and the auricles and flowing, and multitude of sleep, and pain of teeth, and of goiter, and generally of all illnesses that come by coldness, thus with paralysis, apoplexy, and likeness in those illnesses.
The form of this cautery is that first of all you command the patient to be evacuated by laxative medicine of the head purging, for three or four days, according to the strength of the patient and his age and custom.
And then command him that he shaves his head with a razor, and then let him lie between your knees on a low bench, and let him rest his feet on you.
And then pause the edge of your palm close to the nose between the eyes. But yet, when the point of the middle part is reached, sign that place with a tent, and then heat the cautery olive of which this is the form.
And then pause it over the point marked by the tent, in such manner that the hand be stretched little by little, and you revolve him.
And then lift your hand lightly and look at the place, and if you see already some part of the head discovered, as well as any amount of bones, then lift your hand again, and if it does not return to you with that iron, with another one, if it is cooled off, between while be seen by you what I have said.
And then take a little salt and dissolve it on the place and let him lick that for three days.
And then pause over it cloth drenched in vinegar and let him lick that over while the scar of the fire is destroyed. And then cure the place with four-ingredient ointment, so that it is healed.
And they said that when the Roman plaster is open, as many meals give heat, for it is better and more healing.
And they said some of them that the jaw be cauterized within the bone, and it is held the cautery within while some part of the substance of the bone is burned.
And then let him lick that which is burnt in the bone, and then let it be cured.
Others say that when the cautery reaches the bone it produces a strong impression on it, and that this is the way to treat small ulcers. And they believe that the vapors of the head are expelled from that place.
And if a wound is left open for a long time, it should be treated until it is healed and consolidated.
But I have not seen these two species of cautery at all, except in some men according to the way of fear; and that which leaves, by my opinion, is better for health when it is; because the head is devitalized by solution of continuity in it also as we have testified in other members, and mainly when the head of the patient is of a phlegmatic nature.
And the species of the first cautery is more safe and better by my opinion; and with it we use and act for health.
Chapter second.
Of the cautery of the head.
When in all the head there happens chronic and long pain and this is prolonged in the patient, and he uses herbs and clysters and caput medusae and plasters and cataplasms and lances and poultices and hot stones and similar remedies, and mainly if he has already been cauterized with a cautery which we recount and does not benefit him any of those causes, then consider that if the head of the patient is of strong creation in its nature; and it is phlegmatic and finds great heat, then cauterize with another cautery after that one a little. And then cauterize that above the horn of his head with a cautery until the membrane is split. The membrane being split and the quantity which we have recounted being discovered from the bone, cauterize that with a cautery in the posterior part of the head in the place which is called vas, — and it is that place in which the cupping-glass is applied. And hold your hand over that, and do not discover the bone, because the patient by that finds much greater pain than from the pain of all the other cauteries of the head.
And I say to apply this cautery in its place, because the cautery with which you cauterize the horns of the head and the occiput is a more subtle cautery than that with which the middle part of the head is cauterized; and it is applied as follows:
Chapter third.
Of cautery of not antique emigration.
When suddenly in the anterior part of the head there is a painful swelling, or the pain extends to the eye, evacuate the head with purging medicines, and administer the other cure, which I have described in the chapters on diseases; and if all does not benefit, cautery is applied to it in two ways: either cautery with an acute medicine burning, or with iron.
But cautery with a burning medicine is that you take an almond, and scorch it and rub the ends of it on both sides of the head. And then pierce the place of the pain in the temple with a pointed lance until it is made in it beneath the membrane, as far as it can be felt.
And then press on it with a bandage tightly bound, and leave that for the space of three hours; and then remove the bandage and treat the almond, and let the wound for two or three days, and then apply to it oil sprinkled with alum as far as the place makes blisters.
And then cure that with an ointment until it is healed.
And if you will, do this with some burning medicines which I have written in the two tractates of burning medicines.
But the cautery with iron is done according to this way: heat an iron cautery of which this is the form:
and it is called claus clavilis, because the head of it is like the form of a nail in which there is some curve, and in the middle part of it is a small prominence.
And then apply it to the place of the pain, and hold your hand — so that the cautery which is beneath is not touched — and move the iron little by little with speed.
And if the quantity of it that is burned by the thickness of the membrane as far as the size of it, and raise your hand so that the artery which is beneath is not touched, so that there does not come a flow of blood.
And then moisten a cloth in salt water and apply it to the place, and leave that for three days; and then apply a cloth moistened with wine, and cure with an ointment until it is healed.
And if you will, cauterize with the point of the scalpel according to the cautery, and beware of incision of artery in this not antique emigration properly.
Chapter fourth.
Of cautery of antique emigration.
When you cure emigration with what we have said of the cure preceding, and what we have said in the chapters on diseases, and the cure does not benefit, and you see in the disease that it does not suffice to it what we have said of the first cautery with medicine or of the cautery with fire, then when you ignite the cautery cutler until it is whitened, then indicate over the place of the pain with a line of length of which is the size of the digit, or as much as that; and laying your hand by one side, and piercing it into the artery and coming to the bone.
However it is necessary to you that you guard against the continuation of the jaw, which is injured because of mastication, and that the ligament not be burned and the nerve which hurts that, and that no spasm come upon it.
And if it is about the custody and care of flow of blood from the artery which is incised, because in the incision of it there is danger, and mainly to him who ignores what he does and is inexperienced and unskilful; and let the operation begin in that place.
And I will come with remembrance of the regimen of flow of blood from the artery according to his manner, in that free space.
And if you see of this disease that it does not suffice this cautery and see the body of the patient tolerable, cauterize that in the middle part of the head as we have recounted, and cure the wound until it is healed.
And if you will administer the cautery which we have said in the chapter of incision of artery with cautery having two points, and this cautery is better and more suitable.
Chapter fifth.
Of cautery of pains of ears.
When in the ear there is pain from friction and it is cured with lactic causes and with the other cure which I have said in the chapter, and the pain is not relieved, then ignite the cautery, and this is the one which has the name puncta, of which this is the form:
And then puncture it with the point and carry it around the whole ear as it is turned, or in the circuit of whichever part if the pain is in whichever. Long it with the cautery of the edge of the ear few by few until you feel the place with touch.
And if the cautery of ten points in all the ear, and those around it, and then cure the places until they are healed.
Chapter sixth.
Of cautery of torture.
Torture which is cured and by cautery is not excepted from the remedies which come through phlegm, according to what we have said in the chapters on diseases.
Avoid cautery of the part that hurts due to dryness or due to a spasm in the nerve.
When you treat this kind of torture with potions and bloodletting and poultices, and your treatment does not help, then you should cauterize the patient with three cauteries: in the first place, you must cauterize the root of the auricle; in the second place, a small cautery below the temple; and in the third place, you must cauterize the junction of the two lips.
And apply your cautery on the side that hurts, because softening only comes to the part that appears to be healthy.
And the way to do cauterization is that you must cauterize the auricle on the right side of its upper extremity a little above the horn of the head, and another one in the temple, the length of which should be according to the length of the finger toenail; and you must apply your hand with the cautery until half of the thickness of the cord is burned.
And this is the form of cauterization, and it is a specific of the cutler, the shape of which is like a table knife. But indeed more subtle is that one a little bit so; and it is necessary to cut in him of superficial grossness a little bit.
And then treat the place with what is before prepared until it is healed.
Chapter .VII.
Of cautery of ancient apoplexy.
When apoplexy is ancient and you treat it with what we have said, and your medication does not help, and the patient has no fever, then you should cauterize him with four cauteries: over all the horns of his head; and with a cautery on the middle part of the head, as we have said before; and with a cautery in the neck. And the way to do cauterization is done according to what is above said.
And it is cauterized over the mouth of the stomach; and it is more behind; and then it should be treated with what is prepared.
Chapter .VIII.
Of cautery of oblivion made by flame.
And you should give the patient at the beginning large potions and purgative pills.
And then scrape the whole head of the patient and apply on the neck of him plaster of cedar described in the treatise of plasters.
And apply that some times, for that is the way to do cauterization. And do that according to that medicine which I have said before.
And if he is healed by that well, and if not, then do to him three cauteries in the back part of his head, which descend from the uppermost part of the head to the lower part of the neck. And pause between each cautery the thickness of a finger, and then treat the cautery with what is prepared.
But if you see that he can tolerate it and the patient is that strong, then do to him cautery in the middle part; and if you see greater strength, then do cauterization on both horns.
Then treat that until it is healed; and let the cautery be olive oil according to the form before given.
Chapter .IX.
Of cauterization of hernia and of softening of the whole body.
And you should process cleansing of the head with potions and with what we have said; and then scrape the head of the patient, and then cauterize him with cautery in the middle part of the head, and with cautery on all the horns of the head, and with cautery on the back part of him, and with three cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck.
And if it is necessary in the softening of the body of hernia and the patients tolerate it, and the illness is strong, then do to him four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and lastly with cautery until half of the thickness of the cord is burned, and lift up your hand. Then treat that until it is healed, and let this be olive oil cautery.
Chapter .X.
Of cauterization of epilepsy.
The epileptic is not cauterized except that epilepsy is due to phlegm.
And then cleanse the brain of him at the beginning with herbs and with the other treatment which we have said in the division when the patient is big and can tolerate the exception of medicines.
And if it is a child who does not endure medicines, then administer poultices and masticators the servant cleansings, before for several days, with the benefit of foods.
And then scrape the head of the patient, and then cauterize him with a cautery in the middle part of the head according to the previous way, and with another cautery on the back part of his head, and on each horn of his head you must cauterize. And if the patient is strong and can tolerate it, then do to him cauteries which I have said, having paralysis and softening of the body on the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back.
And let the cautery be olive oil according as it is before.
But if the patient is a child, then apply subtle cautery according to this way.
Chapter .XI.
Of cauterization of melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupt humidities and phlegm, then do to him cauteries which we have said in having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is excess phlegm declining into melancholy, and the body of the patient is cold, then give to him to drink what cleanses the brain of him according as it has been said in the division.
And then scrape the head of the patient, and then make a decently made sponge of lye on the circle, and then apply it in the middle part of the head.
And the patient must be lying down, and he must hold his entire body.
And then apply linen; and it is also worthy of lamb's wool. And heat that over the fire with moderate warmth by measure, which the patient can endure when he is in him. And then apply it in the middle part of the head in the circle, and wash it when it is cool.
And do that to him once every week for one day, and let him have the other regimen of him well until it is healed; or if you want, cauterize him making small points according as he can endure them, except that you must hold your hand over a cautery in this way arranged: this is a specific cautery which softens the brain with equality.
And then place that cut part in a bath of warm water or in a bowl of rosewater.
Chapter XII.
Of cauterization with descending water.
When you have observed the beginning of water in the head through the signs which I mentioned in the division, then begin and give to the patient something to drink that cleanses his head, and guard him against all humidity.
And let him bathe in warm water for several days.
And then command him to wash his hair, and cauterize that with a cautery in the middle of the head; and also cauterize that with two cauteries over the temples if it is the beginning of water in both ears, or on one side if the water begins in one ear.
Cut with a cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the collarbone; and the cauteries should be in that length in the breadth of the temples.
And guard against bleeding when it is cauterized; and if you see any bleeding from him, stop it with some medicine which is possible for you.
And I will come with wisdom which is in the extraction of arteries and with abstention from those and cauterization to prevent bleeding.
And sometimes it is cauterized in the nape under two bones with two cauteries recently produced.
Chapter XIII.
Of cauterization of old tears.
When tears from the ears are long-standing and persistent, and through the veins and arteries which are in the most obvious location on the head, it is verified that this is an excess of phlegmatic moisture, then cauterize that with a cautery which we have recounted in the chapter on the beginning of water coming into the ears, and with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with two cauteries on the nape under two temples, and with two cauteries on the nape under two bones. And if you see any discharge of matter, then cauterize that in every part of the ear canal at the end of the upper jaw with a small cautery.
Chapter XIV.
Of cauterization for fetor of the nose.
When you are treating someone with what we have said in the division and your treatment does not prove beneficial, then prepare and give the patient enemas for three nights; and then shave his head, and cauterize that with a cautery made of olive oil. And also cauterize that with a cautery of cloves with two cauteries over the two upper jaws under the hair, a little one.
And guard against the artery so that you do not ignite it.
And of the cautery of cloves this is the form.
Chapter XV.
Of cauterization for softening eyelids of the ears.
When the eyelid of the ear is softened by sickness or humidity, then cauterize that eyelid with one cautery with this cautery of the moon; and this is its form:
And if you wish, cauterize that over the two upper lids a little with two cauteries all around, and they should be elongated from the temples. And let the length of each cautery be according to the amount of the eyelid.
And do not press too hard with your hand on the cautery, but according to how much the upper part of the eyelid is swollen.
Chapter XVI.
Of cauterization for the eyelid of the ear when hairs have become ingrown and pierce the inside and poke the ear.
When the hairs of the ear become ingrown so that they pierce the inside and poke the ear, there are two ways to cauterize them, either with a cautery of iron or with a cautery of burning medicine.
If you cauterize it with fire, command the patient to wash his hair so that he does not hurt himself when he cuts off those hairs, until they are long and smooth; and if the ear is punctured by them, then strengthen his ears with a bandage so that he is not hurt as the hairs grow.
Thus when they grow and are smooth, then put the patient's head in the warm water, and then sign on the eyelid of the ears with a mark, a sign which is according to the figure of a dead leaf, and let the beginning of that sign be near the hairs.
And then put paste made with white vinegar or mullein on the ear.
And then ignite the cautery of which this is the form:
And then cauterize over the figure which you have marked, bit by bit, in small circles, until the surface of the collarbone is burnt up which is as it were with a myrrh leaf, all appearing properly.
And the sign of health of your work is that you see the eyelid of the ear already contracted and the hairs of it raised above the puncture of the ear.
And then lift your hand and let him go for three days, and then put on him paste made with oil until the scar is healed. And then cure that with ointment until it is healed.
But if they return for any reason and the eyelid is softened, then do again the cautery on that all around as you did at first.
But if the hairs are under the eyelid, then cauterize that until it is raised to its natural place and is smooth and the hairs do not poke the ear.
But the cautery with burning medicine is that you command the patient to wash the hairs until they are long and smooth, and then let the cautery be made of linen in the form of a myrrh leaf.
And then take some boiled lye and live coal mixed with it. And you shall take some boiled lye and live coal mixed with it. You shall take that mixture and add to it some live coal, and make that into a poultice so that it is not cold; and then spread that on the cloth which is made as the form of a myrrh leaf, and put that on one or both ears; and let the patient's head be in the warm water, and his hair in its natural position.
And hold the cloth over the medicine and press it gently so that the patient does not feel the biting of the medicine, for the biting is in him as with fire.
And when you perceive that the biting has ceased, then take away the medicine and wash the ear with water; and then consider if you see the eyelid raised as it is washed or as a result of being bound up with fire or with an incision, for then it will be well; and if it returns over that on which the medicine did not work its effect and does not darken until your operation is healed and the ear contracted.
And then put on it paste made with vinegar of wine or with another ointment until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you, after your operation that you watch with great diligence that no pus comes from the ear, and if the eyelid after several days is softened and some cause of the hairs poking in the ear, then repeat your medicine on that location of the eyelid which is softened, and particularly as you did at the beginning, and bandage him up until it is healed.
And this is the form of a myrrh leaf.
And know that the bodies of men are diversified according to size and smallness, and therefore according to this is made your contraction.
Nor is it hidden from those who follow this path that it is studied in this art.
Chapter .xvii.
Of cauterization of a fistula that is in the tear duct of the eye.
When you are treating a fistula and have not had success with what we have said in the divisions of diseases, then you must cauterize it as follows: order the patient to put his head on your lap, and have someone else hold the patient's head still between their knees so that he doesn't move or shake his head.
Then place a cotton wad soaked in vinegar or in a poultice of poppies over the tear duct.
And heat the cautery, of which this is the form:
which must be hollow, as it is shaped like a reed or a pen made of vulture feathers, from one end of which the cautery is made.
And if you wish, it may extend into the other end. And if you want, it can go out like a tent.
But that which is hollow is better for your work.
And press the fistula if it is open and draw out from it pus and dry it up. And if it is not open, then open it and extract the rottenness from it.
And apply the cautery, which should be well heated, to the eye at the start of the nose so that your hand does not tremble or the patient become disturbed, and then apply the cautery to the edges of the tear duct and corrupt it there.
And so if at the beginning of your cautery it pierces into the bone, that is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery once or twice as necessary, and leave it there for three days, and apply a poultice of dry powder over it until it is healed.
But if eleven days have passed and it has not healed, then apply a corroding acute medicine so that the bone is uncovered and scrape it according to what is convenient in its chapter.
And there is another way to cauterize a fistula which some first said: enter the site of the fistula and open it and then place in that fissure a subtle bed of which its shape is as follows: melt an ounce of lead into it; and hold your hand steady with good control so that the patient does not move, and do not let the melted lead reach the eye of the patient; and place over the eye of the patient a cotton wad soaked in vinegar or water, for the lead will adhere to the site of the fistula and heal it by a wonderful cure.
And if the fistula is healed by what we have said about cautery and cure, that is good; and if not, then it is necessary to apply a tracheotomy and reduce the fistula in the nose according to what comes into its proper place.
Chapter .xviii.
Of cautery of the split of the ear.
Many times fissures occur in the lips and mostly in children.
Therefore, when you treat those fissures with what we have said in the divisions and your cure is not effective, then heat a small cautery knife according to this shape that it fits into the fissure:
And its cavity should be according to the thinness of the blade.

And then heal that with ointment until it is healed.
Chapter .xix.
Of cautery of a fistula in the mouth.
When in the root of the uvula or on the palate or on the roots of the teeth there is an abscess and it becomes swollen, and when it is burst, and when it is old, and is corroded, and a fistula is made, and you cure that and your cure is not effective, then know that you should heat cauteries according to the amount that is received in the fistula, and then apply the hot cautery into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the iron reaches the depth of it, and do this once or twice; and heal that with what we have said about cure until it is healed.
And so if the pus is discharged and it is healed, that is good; and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the site and scrape off the rottenness according to what comes into its chapter.
Chapter .xx.
Of cautery of teeth and of softening of ulcers.
When the ulcers are softened by moisture and the teeth are shaken, and you cure those with medicines and your cure is not effective, then have the patient hold his head in your lap, and heat the cautery of which its shape will come next, so that you apply the poultice over the tooth and insert into it the hot cautery quickly, and hold your hand steady so that the patient feels the heat of the fire on the root of the tooth from which it is coming.
And then lift up your hand and repeat the cautery several times according to what you wish.
And then the patient should gargle with salt water and keep it in his mouth for an hour, and then spit it out, for the shaken tooth is made firm, and the soft gum is made strong, and the rottenness is dried up.
Chapter .xxi.
Of cautery of toothache.
When toothache is from coldness, or in it is aching or green, or the cure does not work with medicine, then the cautery on it is according to two methods: either cautery with cow's dung, or cautery with fire.
Cautery with dung is that you take cow's dung and boil it in a pot made of iron, and then pick up a piece of cloth and wrap it around the end of the needle, and then dip that in the hot dung and apply it quickly to the aching tooth so that it becomes cold.
And then repeat that several times until the strength of the fire reaches the roots of the teeth.
And if you wish, dip wool or cloth in the dung above, and apply it to the tooth that hurts, and place over that hot iron so that the iron reaches the depth of the cavity of the tooth.
But the cautery with fire is that you take a needle of iron or of steel, and there is in it some thickness and the acuteness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
Then heat the cautery of which its shape will come, and apply it to the tooth and hold your hand so that the cautery is cold; and do that several times because the pain usually remains or in that day or in the other day.
And know that by force of that cautery that the patient fills his mouth with good breath and keeps it for an hour, then spit it out, and this is the form of the cautery.
And you cauterize by which you see the end according to what is possible to you.
And this is the form of the needle:
Chapter 22.
Of cautery of excrescences.
When excrescences are of phlegm and of cold humors and they do not yield to digestion with medicines and you see the digestion of those slightly, then heat a cautery whose shape is as follows: having two ends hollow so that smoke comes out from the cautery through one end, and apply it ignited over the excrescence once, and if you need, then repeat it, until it reaches the depth of the excresence.
And if the boil is small, then apply the cautery according to the size of the boil, and let it burn for three days, and place a poultice on it made from boiled oatmeal, until what the fire has burnt is healed.
Then treat this with ointment and bandages and linen until it is healed.

And cauterize this with another cautery behind the junction of the neck at his last vertebra. And the cautery for him should be a red-hot iron according to the previous manner.
Then treat this with what has been mentioned until it is healed.

Chapter 25.
Of cauterization of the tics, which is the head of the helper.

And take the cautery having two points; and this is its form:
And cauterize the windpipe so that it penetrates to the other side; and the figure of cauterization will then be in the form of a cross with four cauteries.

And if the dislocation is to the upper parts and it has been done, then cauterize over the muscle with a red-hot cautery or with many pointed cauteries, for the joint is made firm, and the humidity is driven out and the patient is healed.
Chapter 26.
Of cauterization of the stomach.
When there comes in the stomach churning and many humidities enter so that these are extracted from his complexion and multiplied in him, and if you continue the manners of cure and do not confer with each other, then let the patient lie on his back, and extend his arms and legs, and cauterize this with three cauteries: with one cautery below the feet according to the quantity of a finger with a red-hot cautery, and with two cauteries below the ribs of the cautery so that the figure of cautery becomes triangular; and stretch between these which are not adjusted so that they will make heat.
And if the depth of the cautery is the quantity of two-thirds of the thickness of the windpipe.

Chapter 27.
Of cauterization of the fretted liver.
When there is liver pain because of coldness or because of humidity or because of grossness within so that from his normal complexion there has been produced by egression in excess, and it is cured the patient with what we have said and do not confer with each other, then let the patient lie on his back over his spine, and feel with tent three cauteries according to this form and this quantity pressed upon the liver below the hypochondria where man lies.

And take care that you do not proceed too far in cauterization, and let the windpipe be burnt all through so that it reaches into the bowels, for the windpipe here is subtle; and know this.
Chapter 28.
Of piercing of an abscess of the liver with cautery.
When there is excision or abscess in the liver and you want to know whether this abscess is in the flesh of the liver or in its tunic, then if it is in the flesh of the liver the patient will have heavy breathing and the pain will be sharpened.
And if it is in the tunic of the liver, with great pain and often the physicians have become tired of curing him.
Therefore let the patient be laid on his back; and feel the place of the abscess with tent; and take the cautery which is assembled like a rake, the form of which has preceded in the other page. And cauterize it with this cautery so that all the windpipe is burnt, so that it reaches into the diaphragm, so that phlegm emerges.
And treat this for the cure of other abscesses until it is healed.
And let whoever uses this form of cautery use only that which he has studied in the art of medicine, and through the marks of which many illnesses have become known to him; but let this be tried a few times over this operation, but nonetheless it is better.
Chapter 29.
Of cauterization of sores.
The ancients say cautery of the roots of aristology is applied to sores according to this manner: it is that you take from the roots of aristology a long root which is found, and it should be as thick as a finger.
And then you submerge it in oil and heat it up, and then cauterize with a cautery on the location which is between the continuation of the furcula to the neck; and use two small cauteries guided slightly downward from the part that is below the beard, and use two cauteries on what is declining between the fifth rib and the armpit, declining slightly to the rear parts; and use another cautery in the middle location of the foot; and use another over the stomach, and use three cauteries of the rear parts; and use a cautery in that location which is between the two shoulders, and use two cauteries on the sides of the feet, below the cautery which is between the two shoulders.
And let whoever grasps the cautery with his hand, not close it in the grip of the fist but rather in the open grip.
And some ancients say that some of the people who use cauteries of iron similar to a needle, ignite it and put it in that location which is between the ribs, until we reach with it to that apostema and there be discharged a healthy pus, as we have said regarding the apostema of the liver.
But in this piercing with a cautery there is no fear, for one dies suddenly when it occurs in the location of a fistula to which there is no remedy.
Chapter 30.
Of the cauterization of the melos.
When you cure the illness of the melos with what we have said regarding the cure in division and do not confer your cure, then cauterize it according to three methods, all of which are straight, one of which is that you make three or four lines according to the length of the melos according to the figure of the cauteries of the liver, the figure of which has preceded.
And let there be between each cautery the thickness of a finger or a little more, and the manner of the cautery is the same as we have said regarding the cautery of the liver with equal parts.
And do not grasp the cautery with your hand, and let the patient be on his back.
And there is another manner of cauterizing, which is that you ignite the cautery having two layers, the cause of which we have said in the chapter on dislocation of the muscle, and elevate the tendon which is in the end of the melos through which passes the jaw of the patient on the left.
And let your elevation with which you elevate the tendon be according to the length of the body, so that there are made cauteries according to the breadth of the body.
Then insert the two layers, ignite them, into that location through which you penetrate the tendon on the other side.
And then extract the cautery; and thus there are made four cauteries.
And if you wish, cauterize with a cautery having three layers.
And then you cure the cautery when it has stayed for many days, for indeed the other causes precede in the cure.
Chapter 31.
Of cauterization of hydrops.
Cautery does not cut into hydrops but rather incises it properly.
When you cure hydrops with the manners of cure which we have said in division and do not confer your cure, then cauterize it with four cauteries around the ombelicus and a cautery over the stomach, and another cautery over the liver, and another cautery over the melos, and two cauteries between the shoulders of the back, and a cautery on the right side of the foot, and another cautery over the stomach. And the quantity of the depth of the cautery should be proportionate to the thickness of the tendon.
Then let the cautery remain open so that it may heal for a long time.
And do not discharge the patient from cure after cautery so that there may be added to him two intentions and he remain sick with him through the help of the cure.
The form of the cautery with which the belly is cauterized should be round according to what is above it, and that with which the back is cauterized should be oval according to what precedes it.
Chapter 32.
Of cauterization of feet and thighs.
When the feet are apostemized in hydrops and they are filled with yellow water, then cauterize the feet on the top of the foot in the space between the auricular and the annular, and elevate your hand with the cautery and do not twist it; then elevate your hand and do not return it at all, for the yellow water will flow out.
It is the cautery according to this form: then make two cauteries on both thighs, and in each thigh let there be made a cautery with the tip of the cautery blade. And let the cautery be according to the length of the thigh: one from below and the other above the middle part of the thigh, and on each thigh two cauteries.
And let the wound remain open during a long time for a cure so that any water may flow out from it.
Then cure them with those causes which we have said.
Chapter 33.
Of cauterization of body of belly.
When the body of the belly is for chafing and for moisture within which weakens the vertutes, which are in the stomach and in the intestines, and it is cured that with the manners of cure and does not confer, then the patient suffers cautery of the vertue exhiberant, then cauterize it with a large cautery over his stomach according to what has preceded in the cauterization of the stomach, with the cautery of the circle and four cauteries around the ombelicus subtly, and with cautery clavih subtle; and cautery over the alcatenus above the os gran, or two cauteries.

Chapter 34.

Chapter 35.
About cauterization of ulcers, here is the treatment for them.
When you cut into an ulcer, then you should light the cautery that is similar to a ray. Then insert that burning cautery into the ulcer that has been cut open, and hold your hand over it until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which the blood comes.
And do this once or twice; if there are more ulcers, then cauterize each of them according to what we have recounted, and then cure those wounds with ointment until they are healed.
And if you cauterize with a large cautery on someone, it is better to do so later in the day.
Chapter 36.
About cauterization of fistulas that are made by nature in the parts of the body.
When nature does not obey the work which we have recounted in its place, and the patient is distressed by this, then let him be healed by cautery.
Thus when someone sees a fistula in the nature of the body, and it is old, let him draw out the corruption from within and the corrupted moisture; and therefore what is most worthy to be done is to probe that with a thin needle, and then know the quantity of the depth of it by the previously mentioned probing.
Then light the cautery that is similar to a ray. And then insert that burning cautery into this fistula according to the quantity in which you inserted the probe.
And repeat the cautery on that until those corrupted bodies are burnt one or two or three times, according to the quantity of your need.
And beware of burning a nerve or vein; or if the fistula goes toward the cavity of the bladder or the cavity of the intestine, then beware of all those places; and do not do this unless the fistula is in a fleshy place and you think that it does not penetrate.
And then cure the place until it is healed.
And if the place is sealed and those matters have been cut out from it and remain thus for a long time, then know that it has been healed entirely.
And if those matters are not removed from it, then know that it penetrates or in its preon the body is corrupted, or it falls because of those causes from which will come a recollection in its place.

Chapter .xliii.
Of cauterization in the beginning of gout.
Many times this maladie occurs to small children; and sign of the beginning of it in children is that they occur on them constriction in the armpit, in the elevation and the movement.
And they atrode in the last vertebra of the back and of the nails of him that already begins to rise over the other vertebrae.
And then when you see that and want to prohibit, let it be cauterized by cautery which is circle according to this form: that take the cautery over all part of the vertebra equally.
And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery two or three times. Let the points be close to each other.
Then treat the wound within so that it heals with what we have said.

Chapter 44.
Of cauterization for gout and joint pain.
When joint pain is caused by cold humors that infiltrate each part of the body, and pain occurs in the feet, it is customarily called gout by doctors.
And thus when gout from cold is cured with a method of cure and the pains are not reduced, then apply cautery.
And you should cauterize that area around the joint on the foot with a hot cautery tool.
And let the cautery be olive oil, of which this is its form:
And if it is necessary to make points on the surface of the foot, then do so with a pointed cautery. And if the pains spread within the joints or other joints, and it becomes swollen, then cauterize that on each swollen joint with three cauteries or four, all around, with this cautery of olive oil.
And if you need to use the pointed cautery tool, then cauterize it and do not press too hard with your hand on the cautery beforehand, but just stroke around the edge of the joint gently.
And if the pains spread within both joints, then administer the cautery we have described in its chapter.
And if the pains are only in the fingers and it is called sciatica, then puncture around the circles of the nails as they turn, puncture them in two lines.
And if the pains remain in the fingers, then puncture around the circles of the nails on each finger and on the palm of the hand.
And if the pains spread for several days in the joints or muscles, then cauterize each of them all around.
And do not discharge the patient from good treatment and the reception of medicines, for if good treatment is given and the inflammation is discharged with this cautery it will heal, God helping.
Chapter 45.
Of cauterization for breaks.
When a break occurs in the angles and tears the intestines before the skin of the abdomen, and it begins to happen, then you should order the patient to stop eating for his day and to use laxatives so that the tear falls from his belly.

Then heat the cautery tool, of which this is its form:
until it becomes red and warm. Then return the intestine or hernia to its cavity, and place your hand over the area to prevent the intestine from coming out.

Then hold the cautery tool over that and press with your hand with the cautery tool standing straight, and hold it there until you feel the bone of the elbow enter into the hollow of the forearm; and repeat with another application if you have not achieved it in the first application over the bone.
And observe wisely the movement of the intestine at the time of your cauterization, so that you do not burn the intestine so that over the patient it does not come to death or another great malice.
And know that when you with the cautery do not touch the bone, do not continue your operation.
And see to it that the cautery for children is subtle according to their size and age.
Then cure the area of the cautery for three days with wine until the scar of the fire is healed.
Then cure it with other ointments until it is healed.
And let the patient lie on his back for 40 days while the place is sealed and bandaged.
And see to it that you stop his nourishment according to the length of time of his cure which is loosening the skin of his belly and so that the intestine does not come out through the effort of healing.

Chapter 46.
Of cauterization for torsion.
When a pain occurs in any member through compression or concussion and that pain persists for a long time and is not relieved by medicine, then see to it that you cauterize with a pointed cautery tool.

Chapter 49:

When leukoderma is old and does not respond to any of the healing remedies, then you should cauterize it with a cautery lightly according to the thickness of the skin so that the white and color of it are changed, and its color is altered.

Chapter 50:
On cautery for cancer:
When a cancer begins and you want it to stop growing, then cauterize it with a circular cautery around its circumference as it is turned over.
And the wise say that it should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle of it; but I have not seen this, for I am afraid that it would ulcerate, and I have seen this happen some times.
And it is more proper that it be cauterized around its circumference with a circle as we have said, or with many cauteries.

When an inflammation is delayed in ripening, and it is delayed because of the superfluity that produces it, or because of the state of the patient for whom it is, whether he is old and decrepit, of little blood, or because of the time, and you want to hasten its ripening; then cauterize around its circumference with many small puncturing cauteries; then let it be left so that it will hasten in ripening.

Chapter 52:

Corrosion is a decaying that walks in the member, which corrodes it as fire eats dry wood.

Chapter 53:
On cautery for warts and other similar growths:
Many times warts grow under the feet of an old person who is called a claw, and it is a serious cause, deep-rooted, which pierces the foot; and cautery for these is according to two manners: cautery by fire, and cautery by hot water.
But cautery by fire is that you ignite the cautery needle-like and similar to a penny nail, which should be made of iron according to the quantity that contains the claw entirely, and it should have slender edges.
Then place that ignited one over the claw, and then turn your hand with the cautery around the circumference of the claw so that the cautery reaches the depth of the claw. Let him lie for three days until he begins to move his arm. Then poultice that with wild mallows bruised with salt, and place the poultice over that for one night, for that will eradicate it from its roots.
Then heal the wound with flesh-generating ointment until it is healed.
And if it does not become converted, and sometimes it accedes in the surface of the body, mostly in the hands and feet, then you should administer in those cauteries with hot water, and it is that you take a quail of lead or of iron or of a penny needle, and place that over the claw; and then let him get in the quail of hot water little by little, and hold your hand, and you turn that around with all your strength, and push the needle of the hot water into the depth of the claw, and wait for the patient for an hour, and then remove that, for the claw will have been eradicated from its roots.
And thus they come to those within whom they enter, one after the other throughout their body.
Then cure the sores that are caused by the roots of the claws, which are eradicated with ointments which the flesh engenders.

Chapter VI.

Sometimes bleeding occurs from an artery which is cut beneath the plague, or beneath the incision of an ulcer or cautery on a limb, and it is difficult to stop that.

And be careful that you do not burn the nerve which is here, and that it does not come upon the patient any other harm.

And what has been put in the ear shall already be warmed by fire a little. And beware that the cause which you distill in the ear is not too hot, for the medicines of the ear do not endure that.
Chapter 7
Of the treatment of the inflammation of ears.
Some children are born with hernias from the bellies of their mothers, and this happens in some men; inflammation in the middle of the ear is caused by a hernia or by some wound to that part, and sometimes it is in the openings of the holes.
And what happens in the middle, which does not include the pain, is in the most difficult dispositions to heal.
And in that in which you find the pain, look at the ear of the patient towards the sun. And so if you see swelling apparent, open it with a subtle spatula of which this is the form:
If its end in which the breadth is small, of which one part is acute and the other not, and let the spatula be of two sides smooth so that it does not hurt the ear.
And if the inflammation is from flesh grown in the ear or in the middle of it, then open it with subtle tweezers and cut that vigourously until all the flesh is expelled.
And if the inflammation is in the preon of the ear, then take a slender rod and warm it by fire a little, and then insert that into the middle of the ear.
And so if you have seen swelling with what the patient feels with ease because of the weight, relieve the pressure on it with ease; and beware that you do not hurt the nerves of the ear.
Then put on the ear a piece of linen according to the size of the opening which you have wrapped in Egyptian ointment; and do this for several days until you are sure of the hardening of the swelling; or take some and moisten it with water and sprinkle that over it, having threshed and used it; and if you see the ear already puffed up, then pull off that linen and replace it with another which you wrap in cerote made from oil of roses, until the swelling is reduced; and then treat it until it is healed.
But if bleeding happens, then soak sponge or linen in warm water and place it over the ear, and use the other treatment which constricts the flow of blood, which is said in the treatise on distillation.
Chapter 8
Of the treatment of itchiness that comes to the eyelids.
Athezil which comes to the eyelids of eyes some time moist, sometimes dry.

Chapter IX.
Treatment for the swelling that comes to the eyelids of the eyes.
Sometimes there is a swelling in the eyelids of the eyes due to some cause that resembles a growth in strength and hardness, and because of this swelling it is called a growth.
And it is the accumulation of thick humidity in the eyelid, both above and below.
Therefore, the treatment for these is that one should consider whether the swelling comes from something external to the eyelid and is swollen throughout; and the cause of this is le پرخورة.
Therefore, open a slit in that place according to its width, and carefully scrape it throughout to allow the humor to escape; then suspend it with thread and tie it off.
And if the growth is large, then adjust it with a stitch; and treat that until it is healed.
And if it is small, you will not suffer harm from it because the oil of the eye restores and heals it.
And if the swelling is inclining towards the inner parts of the eyelid, then open the eyelid and suspend the growth with thread, another that you prepare for incision, and press it from all sides, and if the eyelid is extended by incision, then this does not matter in any cause.
And you can open with a slit of width and an incision throughout the eyelid, and the hot humor escaping through the nature of the eye; but if the tension is general in the eyelid so that the humor cannot escape through the nature of the eye except by incision, then make the incision, wash the eye with salted water, and treat the place until it is healed.
Chapter X.
Of the treatment of a circle in the eyelid above the eye.
A circle is a gray thing which is engendered in the tunics of the eyelid above, and mainly in infants, it harms those eyes and adds to their catarrh; and they cannot look at the brightness of the sun because of that which causes them to weep.
And because the hot humor cannot escape through the nature of the eye except by incision and if it causes general tension in the eyelid, open the eyelid with a slit of width and scrape it throughout to allow the hot humor to escape.
And there is another method of treatment for that in which the patient rests his head on you, and then he covers himself with a cloth and makes heat, and makes a circle according to the amount which contains arthernach throughout, and then he puts that on it and presses with his hands so that the catarrh is collected in the middle of the circle, and then open in the middle of that humid place with a spatula by making an incision through the width, and the incision should not be larger than the incision made in phlebótomy.
But in the previous case, split the cord all the way until you reach the catarrh, for in most cases, catarrh is reached through the incision according to the form of whitened gray matter.
Therefore, extract it with pieces of cloth which you have wrapped between your fingers to the outside parts and revolve it between the right and left hand until it is dispersed.
And beware that you do not insert in the incision so that with the spatula, you do not reach the eye and scrape it.
But if you do not see catarrh at the beginning of the incision, but you insert a little with ease so that it processes catarrh; and then extract it as we have said before, and then moisten the cloth in water and wine and place them on the place and bind those tightly.
And if someone has torn salt and places it in the cavity of the incision so that what remains of that humidity.
And then treat that until it is healed.
But if pus occurs in the place of the vein, then treat that with soft bandages until it is healed.
Chapter XI.
Of the treatment of a circle in the eyelid below the eye.
When in the eyelids of the eyes, the natural hairs are born under the skin and are old, then those cause illness to the eye and lead to conditions of illness such as constant tears and softening of the eyelids and the membrane beneath them, which is a cause of destruction of the eye called tactinir of the eye, and it is cured in four ways: either by cautery with fire; or with sharp medicine as previously said in the chapter on cautery; or tactinir is caused by incision and suturing; or by cannas as I will say.
And then you will place the head of the patient towards you; lift the eyelid of the eye with your left hand, and if it is lifted, that is good; and if not, insert a needle into that part where there is pus below the eyelid, and push the needle with the pus upwards towards the margin of the eyelid near where the hairs are born, and pull the pus to the top with the eyelid, and release it.
And then probe inside the eyelid below the hairs with a spatulate instrument into the tear duct where it joins the major lacrimal canal and enters the minor lacrimal canal; then extract the pus and place a small piece of cotton or cloth underneath the eyelid, and sign on the eyelid with a tent, forming a shape like a tail fin.
However, the shape should be according to the amount of swelling in the eyelid, because this varies among people; some require that a large quantity be cut out from the eyelid according to the amount by which it is softened.
And then probe with the spatulate instrument along the two lines you have marked, beginning at where the major lacrimal canal joins the minor lacrimal canal. And if your incision is close to the natural hairs according to the thickness of the membrane, it is good.
And then place the probe in one of the two corners of the pouch, and scrape away the entire lining, and with a thread or fine wool, stitch together the two lips, and clean the blood, and adhere what is superfluous of the membranes above the eyelids by applying some viscous substance, if you wish to do so, and if not, don't cure it.
And then let the stitching of the membranes be for three or four days, and then cure it.
And if you want, let the poultice be unsutured, and cure it with something that dries and constricts, because the eyelid is raised due to the sealing of the poultice and the addition of heat; but stitching is better. And so I have said about tactinir.
However, there should be diligence in performing it on the patient, and it is a good operation without fear.
There is another method for tactinir, which is to mark the shape of a tail fin on the eyelid, and then lift the eyelid with three hooks separated and gathered together according to this shape:
But if that is not possible, and the hooks are not available, then take a needle with thread and insert it at the center of the figure, and push the other end near the major lacrimal canal, and the other end near the minor lacrimal canal, and gather between your fingers the membranes with equality, and then with them, lift up your hand with equal elevation, lifting up all of the pouch which has been marked as we have recommended.
And then stitch together the two lips of the pouch and cure it until it is healed.
But if pus occurs due to your incision or probing, treat that pustule with ceronium and similar substances, and with ointment.
And sometimes it happens that the eyelids turn inwards, so then you should use what we have said about incision; but stitching in each case is more artificial.
Tactinir with cannas is according to this form: And it is that you convert the eyelid and split the figure inside according to what I have described; and then with skill, make two cannas or two thin rods whose length is according to the length of the eyelid and whose breadth is less than the breadth of the spatulate instrument. And you have already cut at the ends of some parts where you hold the threads.
Then gather each one with subtlety beneath what is superfluous of the eyelid of the eye, and tightly constrict the cannas in some parts with strong compression, and leave it for several days; because the pouch will die and become black and rot away, and when it falls, it will push itself out.
But if it is delayed, then break it with tongs, and cure the pouch until it is healed.
And so when it is solidified, the eyelid is lifted and the hairs do not prick.
And this is the form of two cannas which you will make according to this form: and have the quantity of length and breadth neither more nor less.
Chapter 12.
Of the elevation of hairs pricking in the eye with a needle when the hair is hard.
When there are non-natural hairs, hard and rough and pricking the eyes, then the operation on it is that you take a thin needle and place in it thread of fine silk, and then you gather its ends and twist them in a most subtle manner. And let the length of the hairs be the quantity of a palm.
And then you compose another thin thread under it in a short manner, and twist its ends if you wish to do so.
And then place the patient's head towards you, and let it be near the sunlight so that your work is seen clearly, because it is a subtle and delicate operation.
And then insert the needle at the root of the hair which needs skill, and make it penetrate the eyelid quickly while extracting that above the natural hair.
And then pull the hair out from under it and insert it into the eye, and let there be one or two or three hairs at most and not more.
And then pull your hand out with it so that the hair is extracted with the natural hair.
But if it is pulled out with the thread and the hair is not extracted, then pull out the thread from its parts under the hair which you have composed with that thread, so that when it is pulled out from above, the hair will be extracted with it.
And then examine it with the sight of the eye, because when you pull out the thread and the hair, and it does not stick to the membrane, the eye will be clear, and the clause will go away in two or three days, and the hair will adhere to its place and grow well on it.
And if the hair is longer, then you gather a long hair of the natural hairs, and elevate it with that, or let the one which you have gathered be elevated with it so that it is stretched out and you elevate it.
Chapter 13.
Of the cure of a hemorrhoid which appears in the eyelid above it.
When there is a hemorrhoid in the eye, and it is a contraction of the eyelid when it is contracted on one side or the other, from bad healing of membrane or from incisions or cauterization, and it is called leporina, and this inflammation or is natural or accidental, and it is caused by healing of membrane or from incisions or cauterization, or from similar things to their sick ones.

And the secret to your treatment is that you should not pierce anything which has not consolidated according to its original form.

Chapter .14.
Of the cure of ehacrats which is done on the eyelid:
This alxacrati which is done on the eyelid, which is aptly named vertadierament alxacrati; and it is of two types, either natural or accidental.
But if it is accidental, it is not due to the eyelid itself, but because there is some cold and moist humour in the eyelid which cannot drain in any other way than directly, and alxacrati is named for that which is directly vertadieramente. However, if it is accidental, it is caused by a wound or a tear or cautery or something similar.
And the method of operation for this is that you take a needle with a double thread, and pierce the flesh, and make the thread pass from the tear duct on the left into the one on the right, so that the thread passes through both ends of the flesh.
Then stretch out the flesh at its edges with the needle and sew it up with the needle, and insert the needle with a broad spatula. And so if it returns the shape of the eyelid as it should be, that is good; and if not, take a needle and place it in the split figure, and with that convert the eyelid, and close both slits on either side of the eyelid.
And the ends of the two slits are two angles of the incision, which you have made so that they meet; and an angle is made from them when they come together, and a figure is made from them.
And this figure is a Greek letter: the lambda.
And then cut the flesh to the amount that is the edge of it below it, so that it does not hinder the eyelid.
And then bring the separated parts together and sew them with a thread of wool; and then cure those with what we have said about the softening medicines and the poultices until it is healed.
And if alxacrati occurs due to a wound or a tear or cautery, then you should split with a flat fissure over the hairs of the eyelid as has been described. And then separate with the poultice between two lips as we have said.
In the sum of the speech on the cure of alxacrati when it is above or below, let there be an operation in it, according to how it is prepared for the form of alxacrati; and that is in the form of different dots.
And the wise artisans always prepare in whatever way is possible for them to return the figure to its natural form, or close to it, and that patient according to what suits them from the operation and the instruments in the greatest dispositions.

Chapter XVII
Of the incision of a hernia and of what is born from tight flesh in the hole.
Sometimes in the holes of some people, red flesh is born, and it is above-placed so that it covers the pupil, or it is close to or pressing on the eyelids, and it strongly presses the eyelids against the parts in front, and it is attached like a ball bearing.
The operation on him is that the patient places his head in your lap, and then you open those holes and gather up all that flesh with appropriate threads, and take it with a forceps or basket; and then cut the flesh at its beginning so that everything finishes with the scissors, and be careful of the hole that you do not harm it with your operation.
And your incision should be with that which you use to cut those things, or with a spatula which we have mentioned in the incision of the nail, or with small scissors with which the shape of it is gathered according to what is appropriate in this chapter.

But indeed you should guard against all treatment of the hole by natural or accidental way, doing it with iron, and not put your hand in any of these operations unless you see that that member is suffering that operation.

Chapter XX
Of the reduction of a protruding hole.
When the hole protrudes with its totality and does not occur in the swelling nor decrease, then you should loosen the patient, and then let him hold his breath, and then press on the cervix with a scarification and suck strongly with good suction; and then place liniment which is made of alum and aloe and myrrh, and then cover the plaster on the hole with strong poultices.

And you should stop the bleeding near the wound during both day and night as we have said.

Chapter 21.
Of the beginning of the swelling in the tunica intima.
When there is a rupture in the tunica intima and it protrudes outside the eyelids like the tip of a pea, and it assumes a round shape due to this, and you want to operate on it, then the operation should be performed as follows: You should insert a needle at the base of the intima where the rupture is located, below in the upper part; then you should insert another needle with a double thread in the lacrimal gland, and allow that to penetrate while keeping the first needle in place according to its position. Then you should pierce the area of the double fold and lift it up using the needle, and tighten that thread.

And you should tighten it until it is healed.
Chapter 22.
Of the cure of hawks.
This disease that is called alconatis is nothing but an inflammation that is located in the eye, resembling water that is flowing down and not being absorbed.
The way to treat it is to make the patient sit upright and straight, then take his head in your hands from both sides, and move it so that you can see the inflammation flowing down to the lower parts, then dry it up and prevent it from descending, and damage the light, and the patient should see the cause just as he did before.
And if it does not flow down, you should know that it is water.
But if the inflammation is not prepared to flow down by what we have said, then make the patient sit between your hands, and take a thin spatula and place it on the skin covering the tiny space between the conjunctiva and the cornea in the limbus (in that area where the white of the eye joins the transparent part), so that the inflammation can be pushed out.
Once it is pushed out, then you should distill water into the eye that has honey mixed in it, or water in which you have boiled fenugreek and honey.
And you should cure it with the other causes until it is healed.
