Chapter .65.
On the treatment of intestinal hernia.
The advent of this hernia is by incision that extends in the hollow over the belly from parts of the anus of the belly, because loosening the sacs of that rupture towards some of the sacs.
And this rupture is either of the capsule or of the sac; and these two species occur for several causes: either by impact, or by drops, or by noise, or by elevation of some cause serious, or by similitude.
And the sign of that, when it is by extension of the capsule, is that it occurs little by little in a long time, and does not occur suddenly, and it is an abscess that enfolds within the sac so that the capsule compresses the sac.
And the sign of it is when there is a cut on the head, for at first it causes violent pain suddenly; and there is an apparent pustule beneath the skin, and this is due to the hernia coming out through the opening in the head.
And sometimes the intestine has slipped out of its covering, and this hernia is called intestinal hernia.
And sometimes it is caused by windiness, and sometimes the intestine splits open and there it is retained, and this is a great harm to the patient; and sometimes it causes terrible pain especially when pressed upon.
And in the treatment of this illness one must be wary of using iron because it is likely to cause damage in that place.
And the way to perform the operation on this is to command the patient to withdraw the intestine with his hand to its openings inside his cavity if he obeys its return, and then to have him lean back between your hands and raise his legs.
And then tighten the scrotum which closes the scrotum of the testicles at its upper openings, and insert the testicles all along its length; and press on two lips of the incision with hooks according to how you direct them to open the incision with those.
And if the incision according to the amount that is possible for you, then may some of that hernia have slipped out.
And then scrape away the brain matter which is beneath the scrotum of the testicles, while the white hard brain at each opening is exposed.
And then you insert your finger into that which closes the testicle, into that which is between the white brain and the scrotum of the hernia; and clean away with that adhesion which is in the opening behind the hernia.
And then stretch the scrotum of the testicles at its openings, and with the left hand stretch out the white brain to the sides, and lift up the hernia with the brain to the opening of the incision; and command a minister to stretch the hernia out and you dissolve the adhesion which is behind with a complete solution.
And check with your fingers that there is no cause for the intestine to be wrapped up in the white hard brain. But if you find any cause from him, then you cover it with a cloth beneath his belly.
And then insert in the opening beneath the scrotum of the testicles through which blood and pus flow as we have described before.
And then administer wool soaked in oil, and place it on the wound; and administer the sewing which we have recommended (and sometimes the white brain is cauterized which we have said before the incision of it fear the flow of blood because in many times they occur there) and leave the sewing so that by itself it falls.
But if the healing of it is delayed then oil should be applied to the water and placed on that so that it falls according to what we have said.
And then cure the wound with the other cure of wounds until it is healed.
Chapter .lxxxvi.
Of intestinal hernia.
In this hernia I have not seen anyone who has been healed by its treatment with iron.
And the first one said that it is made like we have recommended in the hernia which is with wine; and the other is to sew the vessels above the incision on that with ease of it; and then dry in the middle place around it as you open the apostema with what causes it, while the vessels fall.
And cure the wound according to what we have said until it is healed.
Chapter .lxxxvii.
Of the separation that is made in the joints.
Sometimes there is a rupture in the joints as we have said and it emerges from the place.
And do not let any cause of the intestines come to the genitals; and if it comes it is little; and return in all hours.
But if the time is prolonged with that then it is a fissure in the brain which extends from the scrotum into the brain; and this happens because of the extension of the brain which is in the joints as we have said, and then it becomes soft and the place is apostemata and emerges.
And its cure is with cautery like that which precedes its narration.
And sometimes it is cured with iron in this way: and the patient leans on his back between your hands, and then dry the place of the rupture of the apostemata which emerges with an incision according to the length of three fingers.
And then strengthen the white brain which is beneath the scrotum so that it is exposed.
And then take the thread and place that over the prominent place of the brain, and press that against the bone of the belly.
And then cut the two prominent places over the extremity of the thread of the brain, and join with sewing one of those to the other.
And then cut off the extremity of the thread, and do not insert from the brain at all, nor stretch out the hernia, nor another cause as you have come to know in the cure of intestinal hernia.
And then cure that with the cure of wounds, and when you insert the threads, cleanse that and restore the wound until it is consolidated; because the brain is contracted and not adjusted to the eminence of the rupture.
And cautery is better in this place because it is closer to health.
Chapter .lxxxviii.
Of softening of the scrotum of the testicles.
Many times the scrotum of the testicles in some men is softened because the flesh which is between that is softened, and is felt the guarding of it.
Then it is necessary for him who is treated in the cure of it that he makes lean the patient according to his back, and insert all the scrotum which is softened over the natural scrotum; and then sew two lips with sewing.
And if you want in the beginning the superfluity of the softened scrotum with three or four cuts and with firm sewing.
And then insert between the sutures; and then cure by the cure of the other wounds until it is healed and the threads fall.
Chapter .xc.
Of emasculation.
I know that emasculation in our law is forbidden but to me it has been revealed to me that I remind you of it in this book; and it is not necessary for its reminder except for two ways, from which there is one so that that happens in the science of medicine when he is questioned about it, who knows the cure of it to which it happens; and the other way is that we have many times needed emasculation of other animals for our young ones by those, as of horses, and of oxen, and of pigs, and of like things to the animals.
And so I say that castration is performed in two ways: either by crushing or by cutting with a blade.
However, in the method where castration is performed by crushing, the procedure is to have the animal lie down in a body of water so that its genitals become soft and droop and hang down. Then hold those with your hand so they are resolute and do not appear below the touch.
However, in castration performed by cutting and slicing, one must have the animal and press the cord of its testicles with the left hand.
Then tie the scrotum, and cut through each pair of testicles so that two pieces are produced.
Then cut those again once you have skinned them. And do not let any cause remain over those of the brain, but the subtle brain which is over the vessels.
And this method of castration is better which is performed by crushing because strong crushing will leave no cause from the testicles for the animal to desire sex.
Then treat the wound so that it may heal.
Chapter 70.
Of the cure for hermaphrodites.
Hermaphrodites in men occur according to two methods: the first is where there appears to be a space in the cord of testicles, in that which is between two testicles the shape of a female vulva; and also where there is an opening between the penis and the anus from which white fluid flows.
And sometimes urine comes out of that which is in the cord of the testicles.
But in women it is unique: and that the clitoris of a woman on the penis is like two testicles of a man a little bit at the entrance of the vagina just like the foreskin of a man and two testicles.
And the cure is of three species: two from men and one species from women. And it is that you cut into those tight meats so that the fluid of that flows out, and then cure those with treatment for the other wounds.
And in the second species of men from whom urine flows from that which is in the cord of the testicles, there is no cure nor operation on him.
Chapter 71.
Of menstruation and of prominent meats due to causes in women.
Strong menstruation is constricted due to natural causes so that it is pressed and made short, the womb being guarded; and sometimes it is magnified in some women as much as in men and pervades into sexual intercourse.
Therefore you must have the superfluity of menstruation cut with your hand or with a knife, and cut it.
And do not cut deeply, especially in the vein of the artery, so that blood does not flow out.
Then cure that with treatment for wounds so it may heal.
But a growth is meat that grows in the womb of the mother and fills it up, and often appears at the openings of the vagina according to the appearance of a penis (and for this reason some first called it “tailed hermaphrodite”); therefore we must cut it as we cut menstruation, and cure it so it may heal.
Chapter 72.
Of the cure of hernia.
Hernia is when the clitoris of a woman is not perforated or is small. It can be natural or accidental.
Accidental is through disease which has preceded it, and that is caused by meat growing constricted or by subtle brain or thick.
And it is caused in the womb of the mother or in her ribs or on top of them or at the bottom of her, and prohibits coitus and impregnation and menstruation, and often prohibits urination as well.
And the knowledge of it is caused by observation of the midwife, if the swelling is apparent then you check it with your fingers or with a needle; but if it is not apparent then you pierce it with your fingers or with a needle.
But if the swelling is due to subtle brain and is close to the two lips then you cut it and break it up.
And that is so that you may pause over the two lips with your fingers and also place your fingers on both sides of the mouth to hold it shut.
And the woman should be on her back with her legs spread out and you also spread the two lips with force so that the subtle brain is broken up and the swelling is opened.
And then take wool and dip it in oil and place it on the wound, and apply a poultice every day so that the wound does not close up.
But if the brain is thick and dense then you must cut it with spatium or with myrrh oil.
But if the swelling is caused by growth then suspend it with a needle and cut it up.
And they are the medicines which stop the flow of blood without biting like ahauca and dragon's blood and gum arabic bound with egg white.
And then administer a broad lead rod so that the wound does not heal up quickly.
And keep it for several days and administer hot water from the lyre.
Then it will be healed by other healing methods of consolidation so that it may heal up.
And sometimes they occur in the womb due to the occurrence of other meats and then you must cut according to this method. But if it is due to an ulcerated wound in the womb which has not been made contrary by iron in any way.
Chapter 73.
Of the cure for hemorrhoids and of a tail and of red botches which occur in the clitoris of women.
Hemorrhoids are the appearance of the orifices of many veins from which there flows from them continuous blood; and when hemorrhoids are old and they have become enlarged and swollen.
And I have already mentioned the species of those and their signs, and I shall now mention those which received cure and also those who did not receive cure.
Therefore I say that hemorrhoids and theyls when they are in the womb and do not appear to be felt, then in those there shall not be made cure with iron.
But those which are in the orifices of the womb upon which one feels heat, then they must be cured.
And you must put the woman in a warm bath and then extend the hemorrhoids with tweezers or with an asp, and cut those with scissors.
And then powder the hemorrhoids with one of the powders which stop the flow of blood by biting like ahauca and like its similar to those.
And then pluck her feet for an hour, and then place her in warm water.
And if the flow of blood persists then let her drink a decoction of sumac and of husks of pomegranates and of hulls and of similar things.
And then take flour of bran and comb that hemorrhoid with honey and sour wine and make a poultice with it over the hemorrhoid.
And if the blood is scanty then let her drink a mixture of honey and vinegar; but if not, then have her sit in a bath between two hot stones, and on the hemorrhoid apply escarification with a needle.
And then take wool and dip that in the juice of colander or in the juice of henna or in the juice of holly and let her drink wine that has been cooked with it, and apply it to the hemorrhoid; and then cure the wound so that it may heal up.
And cure that interior part so that it heals.
Chapter 74:
Of piercing a ulcerated wound in the head.
[The following is a list of diseases and conditions that can affect the head:] Diseases of pustules and abscesses occurring in the head, like cranial abscesses, pustular ulcers, suppurative inflammation, herpes zoster, fistulas, blood clots, and other abscesses. And I have already spoken of these diseases and their types and characteristics, as well as their treatments in the previous divisions.
Now we will discuss treatments for the head. [And I will tell you in this treatise about an abscess that appears on the head, which is among the types of abscesses that drain pus. And if you want to know how to perform the incision using a hot iron:]
So you must consider if the pain of the abscess at its onset is sharp with percussion, phlegm, and fever, and if it becomes inflamed and if pus forms on top of it, then do not open it with an incision; instead, treat it with something that aids in ripening until the acute symptoms subside.
If you find that the abscess causes pus and phlegm, and if it hurts with percussion but does not form a lump on top of it, then this abscess is not ripe.  [So you should make the woman lie down on her side with two pillows; recline on your back and elevate your feet to the lowest part of your abdomen, and let your thighs be spread apart, and rest your arms below your elbows, and lean forward at a comfortable angle.]
Then the midwife should follow the right side and administer the instrument through which the opening in the head will be made, the form of which will depend on the causes that are presented.
And as you lean forward at a comfortable angle, follow the right side and administer the instrument through the opening in the head; and when you want to administer this instrument, make sure that your finger on the woman's forehead is pressed against it, and what enters the head from the instrument should not go deeper than your finger and press against the patient. But if the instrument is larger than the opening in the head, then you should place cotton on the texture of the forehead to prevent any instrument from entering the opening in the head.
And if you see that the abscess drains pus, then quickly make an incision over it, and take advantage of what the midwife does to approach so that the incision is not deeper than the opening in the head.  [And place the vertitge (a type of instrument) that runs along the instrument from above, and let the minister hold the instrument and rotate the vertitge as the opening in the head is exposed.]
And when the ulcer appears and is touched with the hand and feels hot and moist, then you should dry that part of the head with a sponge.
And if you see pus in the ulcer and it does not drain quickly, then make a pointed cautery over it so that the ulcer is opened and it is not deeper than the opening in the head.   [And when the pus has been discharged, then place a poultice that has been soaked in rose oil or oil mixed with some astringent; and place the calca7 (a type of bandage) on the section where the ulcer was.]
And place a bandage over the head and on top of the poultice, clean wool that has been soaked in water in which mallows have been boiled.
And if you see that the patient does not drain pus quickly, then make a pointed cautery over the opening in the head so that it is more opened and not deeper than the opening in the head.    [Then let it be cured after two days with an ointment that is suitable for it to heal.]
And sometimes the head and poultice are washed with water and honey, and then with water in which verbena or long pepper has been boiled, and then return to the ointment.
And if the poultice is stuck in the head, then you should be prohibited from treating it with an iron, but instead treat it as we have said in the previous division.
Chapter 75:
To teach midwives how to treat live fetuses according to their appearance when they are born in a non-natural way.
It is necessary that the midwife knows the appearance of a natural childbirth by its characteristics, and when you see the woman expressing the lower parts and desiring to smell the air, and being pressed upon by what is above her, and hastening the birth of the fetus, then you will know that this delivery is according to natural figure, and it is the birth of it on top of her head, and the second one with it hanging or suspended from the umbilical cord.
So when you see these signs, then let the belly be compressed so that the fetus descends gently as it descends over his head, and the second one to him, and is washed of those superfluities with good washing.
But that which is other than this part is unnatural and unworthy, for when the fetus is born on his feet and his body is born before his head and his arms, or when it is born on its side with one arm, or under its feet. Or it is born on its body and its head is born with what is suitable so that the fetus is born on his back and his feet are hanging, or his head is born and his arm, or from his belly and he is turned onto his neck, and resembling those figures of him that are unworthy.
And it is necessary that the midwife be wise and subtle in all those causes, and that she guards against error and deception.
I am showing you all the figures of those, and what skills they have in order to be understood by this and to stand for this.
When the child is born on its head through a natural delivery, and it is violent with the mother and there is difficulty in delivering it, and when the strength of the mother has already been weakened, then make her deliver the child, or if women have it, evaporate its amniotic fluid with fennel and olive oil.
Then the midwife should insert her little finger between its lips and split it with her fingernail, or suck that moisture out of it with her mouth. And press the woman's belly to make the fetus come down.
But if it does not come out, then cover the woman with a poultice of linseed and a poultice of fennel with honey.
Then command the midwife to press it and make the woman sneeze with a seasoning; and put the poultice in her mouth and nose for an hour, because the fetus will come out immediately.
And if both ends of the fetus have not yet come out at first, then cover them with a little ease little by little. But if it does not obey the instrument, then put the woman on a bed and lift her feet up, and then rock the bed on the ground; and the woman should be held so that she does not fall because of the rocking.
And if the hands are not turned inside out and the fetus is dead, then cut them open and pull out the fetus's arm or tie its body to your hand with a cloth and pull it out equally, because that will come out.
When the fetus is on its feet, then you should push those up, and then turn the fetus a little, and then suck it, and then take one of its feet and stretch those little by little.
But when it has come in between the thighs, then you command it to be squeezed out, and make her sneeze with seasoning, because it will come out if God wills.
And if it has not come out with what we have mentioned, then you return the fetus little by little to its natural second position, because that will come out with an easier delivery.
And if it is prohibited by everything that we have mentioned, then take a poultice of alder and dissolved gum, and beat them both well in the mortar, and then line with that the amniotic fluid of the woman, at the bottom of her belly. And then make her sneeze in lukewarm water until she gets rid of the phlegm.
And when his limbs are softened, then make him smoke with myrtle and put that under him. And when she has smoked for an hour, then make her sneeze on a bed, and then suck her mouth and lift from that, and press the bottom part of her belly with a little compression, because the fetus will be delivered immediately.
Delivery of the fetus hanging sideways by one of his hands. It should be understood as a reduction of the hand; but if you cannot reduce it, then raise the woman and make her walk around.
And if she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed, and rock her thighs with violent rocking, and then give her something to drink which you have prepared from poultices.
And when the delivery is complete, then make her sneeze on a bed, and then study the reduction of the hand, and suck the fetus into a natural position, and make the woman sneeze and command him to press himself until he is delivered.
Delivery of the fetus on its neck with its hands and face expanded and his forehead pressed against his mother's abdomen. The midwife should hold the fetus' hand and then roll it little by little, and this will be easier for her.
And when he is born, and after he has been cleaned off, then put on him what we have mentioned of oil and poultices.
And then command him to hold his mother little by little, and when you have done that, then make her sneeze on a bed and command him to be pressed; and make her sneeze with seasoning. Preparation of the fetus delivered sideways.
When they are about to be born from the mother in this way, consider and then you should insert the second one with your fingernail until it is evacuated of moisture.
And if the fetus is suspended over his face and neck, then you should insert it into the armpit, so that it is not held back and delayed.
And then press the fetus into the arm pits so that it rests there according to what you have commanded, and command the woman to squeeze herself several times, and he will be delivered with an easier delivery, if God wills.
Delivery of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that twins are born several times, and some also give birth to three or four, but that is strange and rare; but their causes are natural, and they do not live.
And count them, although they may be multiple, one second one, and they are separated by caesarean section, distinguish those within the membrane in each of their umbilical cords; and some are delivered naturally with an easy delivery, and some are delivered with a non-natural delivery as we have mentioned.
And if they are difficult to deliver and come to what we have said about the non-natural figures, then you should cure them as we have recounted.
And if the midwife is skillful and does this with ease and skill, and with delay, and she is prepared in every way as it was for her from the beginning, bringing health.
Remembrance of that which forms in the womb out of embryos and abortions.
Sometimes they are formed in the mother's womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and even ten, and I have indeed verified that a woman had an abortion of six, and another of ten, all formed, which cause was made by the measurement of the glorious sages.
And all that should be in the science of the midwife who is strong with her to go to that which resembles that, and then pause at that.
Chapter 76.
On the Extraction of a Dead Fet
When you are treating a dead fetus and have followed our advice on the division of medicine and it has not been expelled, and you must use surgery with your hand, then consider whether the woman is in good health and does not suffer from any of the conditions that may cause harm to her. If she is healthy and free of these conditions, proceed with the following:
Have the woman lie on her back, with her head tilted down and her thighs elevated.
The assistant should be on either side of the woman or tied to the bed so that the woman's body does not extend beyond the extraction of the fetus.
Then, moisten the mother's mouth with warm oils and a poultice made from aloe, fennel seed, and linseed.
Then, the midwife should grease her hand with these oils and poultices, and gently insert her hand into the mother, and then circle her hand around the place where the nails of the fetus are.
And when it is in the right position: then consider whether the fetus is ready to descend head first, and then place its nails in its heels, or in its neck, or in its mouth, or on its palate, or under its beard, or in the hollow of its collarbone, or in the close proximity of its ribs, or below its armpits.
But if the descent is over its feet, then in the groin or in the middle of its back.
And make sure to have the nail in your right hand, and place the curve of the fetus in that space between the fingers of your left hand, and insert your hand gently, and place the nail in one of those places we mentioned, until it reaches the desired effect.
And then place and fix another nail in its position, or the third if necessary, so that it is attracted equally, and not extended according to its straightness only.
And let it be pulled apart entirely, so that the extraction of it is eased as it is done in teeth extractions.
And make sure that the extension is softened between them; and if any part of it is retained, then have the midwife grease her fingers with oil and insert those fingers and rotate with those parts that are retained.
Then, if the part of the fetus is out-of-place, then have the nails be moved to a place that is higher; and do this until the whole fetus is delivered.
But if the hand is out in front of the other one, and it is not possible to return it by the contraction of the fetus, then have a cloth be wrapped around it; and then extract that part until it is all delivered, and insert that or in the joint of the hand or in the armpit.
And do this with the other hand and the two feet as well.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or there is contraction during its exit, or there is swelling on its head, then have the midwife insert between her fingers a thorny spatula and split open the head and extract the fluid, or uncover it with an instrument called "alundat", the shape of which will come with the shapes of other instruments in the chapter that comes next.
And do likewise if the fetus has a large head by nature: and then insert it with a sponge or take it up with an awl as we have said before; and then extract its bones with forceps.
And if the head has exited and is constricted by its collarbone, then have the moisture that is in its armpits be poured out.
But if it is not complicated, nor obstructed by its exit, then insert the head immediately as soon as possible for you.
And if the lower abdomen is swollen or there is water inside it, then pierce that area so that the moisture inside it runs out.
But if the fetus is above its feet, then the attraction of it is weaker and the direction of it to the mother's mouth is weaker.
But if it is constricted by the abdomen and armpits, then extract that with a cloth which you will have wrapped around your hand, and split open the abdomen and armpit so that what is inside them runs out.
But if the other limbs are coming out and the head is turned, then have the midwife insert her left hand; but if the mother's mouth is open, then insert your hand into its throat, and circle with that hand the head, and pull it towards the mother' mouth, and then insert in it a nail or two nails, and pull it with those.
And if the mother's mouth is constricted by an ulcer that is happening to it, then do not press on it; instead, administer an infusion of moist and fatty causes. And use poultices; and follow the patient with waters that soften and moisten.
And if the fetus is on its side, then if possible, have it turned; and administer what we said about the living fetus.
And if that is not possible, then let it be inserted in the armpits, and then extracted.
And make sure to not leave any cause inside the second one.
And when you have completed all of your operation, then administer what we said about the cure in ulcers that are happening to the mother.
And if blood flow occurs, then stop it with styptic waters and administer the other cure.
And I have also seen a woman whose fetus was dead inside her, and then on that fire another pregnant woman, and then the dead fire is the other fetus. An ulcer happened to her in the umbilical area; and it was inflated until an open fire appeared, and then the arms started to move.
And I was called to cure him, and I medicated him for a long time, but the wound did not heal.
Then I applied on him some poultices with strong attraction, and extracted from him one bone, and then after a few days, I extracted another bone; and I was very astonished, for there was no bone inside his belly.
And then I thought they were the bones of the dead fetus.
Then I continued to heal the wound, and extracted from him many bones, the woman having had them in her joints for a long time, and already seeing in such a way for a long time, corrected with her a little movement of the arm.
And I did not attribute that to be strange, but in what there is science and aid to what the doctor does with his hand for curing.
Of the forms of the instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
Form of the opening of the mother's mouth.
This is the form of constriction in which the limbs are wrapped, to this constriction there are two virtues on both ends of two bones. But this virtue is that it be made more subtle by constriction, and it be done with ebony or wood of trees.
And let the thickness of each trunk be the width of two fingers and the margin of each one is an inch and a half, and the length of each is a palm and a half; and in the middle place of two trunks there are two joints of that measure trees which are already closed, of which the length is a palm and a few less.
And these two additions should be inserted into the mouth of the mother so that she is opened by them when you turn the two prescribed vertigoes.
Here is another form, even more subtle and finer:
It should be made of boxwood or beech in the likeness of forceps. But at the end of it there should be two additions just like forceps, and the length of those additions should be one palm, and their width should be two digits.
And when you want to open the mother with those, then you should make the woman lean back so that her feet are hanging, opening what is between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument just as you do with forceps equally according to how much you want of the mouth of the mother while the midwife does what she wants.
The form of vertigo that the ancients said:
Form of impellor by which the fetus is pushed:
Form of amsidity by which the great head is contained
And it is assemled to forceps whose teeth in the end, just like forceps, and sometimes it is made long just like forceps whose teeth are like dog's teeth with which it is cut into and contained. Form of few amsidity:
Form of a hook having one spine:
Form of a hook having two spines:
Form of spatula having two ends by which the head is cut off:
Form of two wide spatulas:
All those instruments are exercised, and when they are more multiplied and prepared, the artesian should be closer to his operation and closer to men because of their quantity.
And it is not a sin for you to make those instruments, for the necessity of them cannot be excused.
On extraction of the afterbirth:
When the afterbirth is retained after childbirth, then you should command the woman to retain her breath, and then make her sneeze with snuff, and press your hand over her mouth and nose, and if through that it comes out, good.
And if not, then you take a pitcher and pierce in the lid a hole and place in that herbs burning the mouth of the mother with rosemary and rue and dill and chamomile and Arab scammony and cinnamon and frankincense. All those herbs or some of them should be submerged in water in the pitcher, and place that over the fire.
Then place a reed cannula into the mouth of the mother, and hold that in while the vapor comes into the cavity of the mother.
And then make her sneeze as we have said, and the afterbirth will be pushed out with speed.
But if this cure does not work and it is still inside, then command the midwife to immerse her left hand in olive oil or in myrrh gel and then place that in the vagina and squeeze with that the afterbirth, and when the afterbirth has been found, take hold of it little by little according to rectum position so that the mother does not suffer a violent push. Before, ensure that it is moved to the right and left sides with ease.
And if the mother's mouth is constricted, we have already recommended the cure with snuffing and with medicine of the pitcher with herbs.
But if it is not pushed out with all the causes that we have recommended, then be careful not to tire yourself out by doing that in repetition of abstraction, but rather ensure that what comes out of her mouth lies in the woman's lap, and then anoint that with ointment and tetrafarmacon; for that will make it hard soon enough and will be dissolved and pushed out.
But when she is raised up, there is evil odor to the head and the stomach, and that makes the woman sick; then ensure that she is administered below with smoking and convenient to that.
But some of the Ancients have already been treated with smoking of nasea and dry figs.
Form of instrument by which the woman is smoked for retention of menses and afterbirth:
It should be made of glass or of horn.
And the small end should be placed into the vagina and the wide end over the fire, and the smoking should be placed over the embers of the fire.
And hold that in while the smoking is consumed and repeat another.
On cure of anus of un-perforated child:
Young children and their anuses are not perforated, they only appear subtle and swollen. Then command the midwife to perforate with her finger that swelling; and if not, perforate it with a pointed spatula, and be careful not to touch the membrane.
Then place over that wool soaked in wine and oil; and then cure that with ointment while it is swollen.
But if you fear that it is swollen, then place in the slit a cannula for several days, and hold it when the child wants to defecate.
And then occurs swelling of the anus by hardening of clot or of abscess; then ensure that hardening is cut into, and then it is cured with what we have said of the cure and the lead.
On cure of fistulas which descend from below:
The fistulas which descend in the beginning of below pus is low and thick, those which descend near the anus exit or in the space of one part.
And it is a fistula or more.
And when that swelling is old and hard, and some times it is penetrated by these fistulas to the point of penetration.
And those are pushed out by what is exited from those through exit and by farting; and sometimes the woman suffers pain with that exit, and much fluid exits from them with a fart.
And sometimes from those fistulas some penetrate into the bladder, and into the throat of the vagina; and they penetrate into the junction of the crotch and into the notch of the anus.
And when the fistula is penetrated into the anus and does not penetrate, then you put your finger in the anus, and insert a thin probe of horn or iron into the fistula when it is swollen.
But if in that there is swelling, then insert into it a probe of lead or of horsehair into the fistula while you feel the probe or the hair in your finger.
And if you do not feel that at all or no process of exit nor farting nor swelling, as we have said, then be sure that it is not penetrated, and then try the cure.
And when the fistula is penetrated into the bladder or into the throat of the vagina, then its sign is emission of urine from that and prohibition of it going to that as the location is cured with medicine has been hardened.
But if it penetrates into the joint of the thigh or into the bone and causes pain in the area around it, then the sign is that you should test it by trying to move it here if there is no tortuosity in the bone, and causing pain in the area around the affected part; and that you should apply a poultice to it from time to time; and that it does not respond to that medicine, nor is it consolidated with an ointment.
And in all those penetrating fistulas, there is no cure for all of them; and their cure is toil and vanity of the foolish doctors who are committed to them.
But in those that do not penetrate and are not ancient, healing with iron is expected according to what I have told you, and that which I have already tried.
And it is that the patient holds his hands over his head and lifts up his legs in between them, his thighs are inclined towards his belly, and then you try to insert a probe of lead or of ram's horn if there is tortuosity in the fistula, trying to find the spot where the probe goes in.
And if that feeling is around his neck, then you should insert your finger there into the neck.
And if you feel the probe already inserted into it, pushing itself in discovered, then you should know for certain that it is penetrating; and then do not work on it, for there is no healing in that, as we have said.
But nevertheless some say that it is healed in some men with vinegar.
And the medicine by which healing is expected in him is that you apply a fine cautery according to the size of the fistula, as it has been mentioned, and you insert that ignited one into the fistula until it comes around the neck; and then repeat that two or three times until you know that all those fistulated meats that are like a feather cane are completely burned.
And then heal that with poultices wrapped in cloth until you have burned all those meats that are joined together, and then heal that with medicines that generate and consolidate the flesh, and if it is healed, well; and if not, then it will not be healed at any time by another cure.
And if it enters and does not penetrate into your finger which is in the anus, and between that and the probe there is a slight space of flesh or of membrane, then you cut the skin at the beginning of the fistula, and you dry up the skin, and you see that it dries up by means of the probe, and let it be in the fistula until the incision reaches the place where the end of the probe comes out, and through the probe it is released and cut.
And then cleanse those fistulated meats which are like a quill of feather and from which no cause is seen to come out.
But if blood flows out between you and your operation when you insert those meats, then the millstone which is and the pus which comes out is cauterized with fire or with a sharp medicine; for cautery with fire dries up the two habits: it is the hardening of those joined meats, and the cessation of the blood from the exudation of moistness.
And then heal that with poultices wrapped in cloth or with cotton until the wound feels dry, and then heal the ulcer with ointments which generate and consolidate hard flesh.
And those are medicines in which there is constriction and drying up; when then it is restored, it is already healed and you do not fear iteration.
But if the fistula already pierces into the anus and is elongated from it to the surface of the body, then you insert your finger into the anus and probe with it.
And therefore if you feel the probe and between you and it there is a slight space of membrane or of flesh, and it is close to penetration, then it is not an operation on him but according to way of trust and of hope.
That cause is administered in him one of three ways: either cauterize that as we have said; or dry it up until you can achieve the cavity of him so that you may insert the catheters and the cure is applied; and do not proceed with cutting so that you do not pierce the membrane containing the neck, and that you bring about on the patient the rising of the exudation against his will; and then heal that with what we have said for it heals quickly; or elongate that membrane and cleanse that pus which dries up near the anus as we have said, or with a probe or another instrument of acute extremity, and then cleanse those fistulated meats which are in the incision where you can pierce by means of crusting; and then strive to bring about the restoration of all the ulcer with cutting, and if the orifice of pus above is not consolidated, and the fistula remains open at the anus, and pus flows out more quickly through the patient. And sometimes the fistula is finished in this way: it is when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is on the side of the anus around the surface of the body with the skin and at the edge of the anus, then take a probe of perforated extremity which is prepared like a needle to pierce hearts according to this form.
And insert into that the thread wrapped in wool or around those; and then insert the probe with the thread into the fistula until you achieve the cavity of him.
But if it pierces near the edge of the anus inside, then you pull out that thread from that piercing as you insert your finger into the anus; and pull out the end of the thread and bring the two ends together, and tighten each one, and let it remain like that for a day or two, and when you have pierced the meat with the thread, loosen that so that those meats which are between the two ends of the thread are pulled.
And then heal the ulcer until it is consolidated and healed.
But if the orifice of the fistula is not penetrating, then make it penetrate in whatever way it is prepared for you, unless it pierces into the anus, for it is not for you to do that which would pierce the membrane; and then heal with that which it has healed.
The form of the split spatula with which the fistula is split: its curvature is made acute and the other side not acute, so that you do not pierce that which is not necessary, as it happens.
Of suturing of hemorrhoids in which blood flows in the incision of those.
Hemorrhoids are according to two ways, for either they are between the anus resembling charcoal, or they are as if they were with grease of fat. And they are small and large, and the blood flows from them at all times, and they are moved, and they are outside the anus and on its edges.
But those which are outside the anus are according to the months of a little humidity, from which flows green water or a drop of blood with a continuous body, and they are according to the color of the body.
And the cure for that which is inside the anus is to command the patient to strain and to press in so that the anus dries up and the hemorrhoids appear to you. Then you grab it and suspend it with your nails or whatever you have those by your fingernail, and then pierce them down to their roots.
But if the nails are not held in them by their moisture and softening of them, then take those with an ashen cloth or a twig or a piece of wool, and pull them out with your teeth, and then insert them and pound upon them some powdered herbs over them after the incision, so that they are like cauterization; or cauterize them according to what is preceded in the chapter on cauterizing. And then treat these with the other cure until they are healed.
And if the anus does not obey defecation, then the patient should be anointed with ointment in which there is a little bit of biting substance, and he should be washed with the water that is in the basin, and it should cause the anus to open easily when the patient is squeezed.
But if the hemorrhoids protrude from the anus, then their cause is lighter, and it suffices that you grab them with your finger or that you grab them with a piece of cloth, insert them, and then treat them with what we have already said until they are healed.
And if you have cut them, then you should administer a suture in this way: take the wax wrapped around and insert it into the needle, and then extract the hemorrhoids at their upper parts, and let the needle pierce the root of the other part; wrap both ends of the wax around the part below the needle and crosswise; tighten the hemorrhoid firmly, and then squeeze the wax and take out the needle.
And do this to all of them, leaving one untouched, in order that the superfluous blood flows from it.
Then place a cloth steeped in rose oil or cerate over the anus, and order the patient to rest. And let that remain until it becomes dry; then treat the hemorrhoids with ointment or with another cure until they are healed.
And if they are old and the medicine does not help, then you should scrape them with a spathon or with your fingernail until they become moist and you see blood oozing from underneath, which prohibits their consolidation; then treat them until they are consolidated.
Then you should dry them more vehemently than before, until there is no blood and they are excoriated; then treat them until they are healed.
Know that hemorrhoids, which are also called piles, are a key point; they are not unless round knots according to the color of the body resembling the head of a nail, and they are found all over the body but especially in the lower parts below the feet and the fingers, and because of them you should experience pain.
Then the cause of what is in the circle of the nail should be pricked and held with tweezers or with a piece of cloth, and be pulled out from its root; then treat it.
And if you want, cauterize the second one that is mentioned in the previous chapter.
But warts are small rough round fistulas on the surface of the body, and they often appear on children's hands.
And its cure is that you stretch it and insert something into it, or that you dry it with wax or tar until it becomes dry. And if you want, cauterize it as we have said before, with fire or with sharp medicine.
But a mole is a small fuzzy or hairy lump on the surface of the body found especially on the back, and when it is rubbed, it feels like an ant bite; it is made all over the body.
And its cure is that you take a reed pen or a feather pen, make it very pointed, and place it on the mole so that it contains the circle of the reed pen; then you rotate your hand with the pen so that you insert what is inside the circle of the mole, place it on the back of the flesh, and eradicate the mole from its root.
And if you want, do this with an iron or steel reed pen as follows:
Let the end of the reed be very thin and blunt (so that it is not perforated) and wrapped so that over the finger it looks washed and rotated.
And if you want, cauterize the mole as it is mentioned before in the chapter of cautery.
Concerning the forms of the instruments that are used to give cautery:
Sometimes cautery is done with silver or brass or melted and hammered iron; and sometimes it is done with small or large instruments depending on what they are used for, because the cautery of small children should be small; and of those whose anuses are tight or painful, their cauteries should be small.
The form of large cautery is:
The end of the reed where the pouch is tied should be wide as follows; and it should have a distinction where the pouch is tied like this many times.
And the lower end which is inserted into the anus should be blunt  (so it is not open) like a lion's tooth, getting thinner; and on one side of the reed there should be two holes, and on the other side there should be one hole, and the size of the hole should be according to the thickness of the thread and bigger for the thicker ones.
And let the pouch in which the medicines of animal bladder or sheepskin are placed, and let its root be one palm.
And it should be perforated with many holes as it is rotated; and if the space between the holes is the thickness of the finger.
Then insert into those holes strong tar that is made of ten tar, or wind it with that; and fasten the pouch with that; and when the pouch is placed on it, squeeze the end of the cautery between two distinctions with a strong constriction, and then cauterize with that each hole: But the quality of cauterizing with that is that you fill the pouch with medicine, which should be warmed according to the amount of tolerance of the patient; and take care that it is not too hot nor too cold.
Then the patient should lie on his back, and raise his legs up and place underneath him a board or a plank; then smear the end of the cautery with oil or egg white or mucilage of fenugreek or something similar; and then insert it into the anus easily, and then the minister takes the pouch and squeezes it with two fingers and expels from the cautery all that is inside it with strength until everything in the cautery is evacuated; then take out the cautery and let the patient raise his legs against the wall.
And if the medicine forces him to defecate, he should hold it as much as he can; and if he sleeps with it for a whole night, it is better to wake up.
But if you cauterize him in the diseases of looseness of the belly and he defecates a lot, then you should repeat the cautery until it is healed.
And if in the anus there are hemorrhoids or hard lumps, then let the cautery be very thin and sharp, of the cauteries with which children are cauterized.
Concerning the cure of wounds:
I have already said in the division of the cure of wounds what suited the free part, and I have also mentioned the cure of them with the hand and medicines according to the complement.
Therefore I say that wounds are diversified according to what caused them and according to the place where they happened.
And the causes for which wounds are made are sometimes due to a stone, or insertion of a spear or knife, or a punch with a lance, or a stick, or an arrow, or something similar from many causes.
But the pain that is in parts of the body are like the plague which afflicts the head, neck, feet, belly, or armpits, and resembles those of the limbs.
And I have described the cure for some plagues so that you understand that argument and rule about other plagues.
I will begin with simple plagues of the head, for the memory of compounded ones will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore, I say that when a simple plague occurs in the head and it is not a fracture, then consider: if it is due to a stone or something similar that has broken the skin and there is a large wound that you fear might develop into an abscess, then you should immediately perform a craniotomy and phlebotomy, according to the amount of vertigo the patient experiences if no other reason prohibits phlebotomy, especially if the blood that flows from the wound is minimal.
And perform phlebotomy on the opposite side of the affected area; and let the patient abstain from food and drink, as well as heavy meals.
But if some cause prohibits phlebotomy, then let the patient reduce their intake of food and avoid wine and meat.
And apply to the wound, if an abscess has formed, a poultice soaked in rose oil or wine in which styptic herbs have been infused.
But if there is no sign of an abscess, then apply to the wound, if it is fresh and the air has not changed that powder which I will mention shortly below.
And if the air has changed its nature, then apply some ointment until it is healed.
But if the wound is large or caused by a cut or something similar, and its lips are not closed together by pus, then close them with stitches as I will describe in the section on stitching.
But if the wound is exposed to the bone and there is no retention of pus except for a small suspension, then insert into it and properly treat the wound with medicines and restore the flesh by applying a poultice on the broken skin, and order the patient to abstain from food that is coarse: onions, garlic, and their likes, until it is healed.
And if you find putrefaction in the wound and it does not adhere to the bone, then cut away all that is rotten and throw it out, then properly treat the wound.
But if in these plagues there is an artery or vein from which blood can flow and it is not cut off by medicines, then probe the artery, and if you find it uncut, then insert a sponge or ligature into it; and if necessity compels you to do otherwise than what we have said, then cauterize it until the blood is stanched.
And if these plagues are simple and small, then their cause is usually slight; therefore, you should apply to them this powder which hardens before the air changes it.
And the manner of making the powder is this: take one part olive oil, two parts dragon's blood, and three parts powdered alumen; let all be well ground and sifted, then fill the wound with it and bind it tightly so that it dries over the wound, then coagulate the blood.
And properly bind it above with powder and lint, and do not loosen it as long as the wound is not abscessed, for if you do, the medicine will not take effect.
And sometimes one can make it alone without dragon's blood when you do not have any at hand.
And this method of treatment is done for large wounds when one deems it proper to apply it and the air has not altered them.
And if the air has altered them, especially in summer time, then do not use this powder, but instead treat them as we have said, by applying some soothing ointments, or by making a poultice of wheat flour with water and honey so that it becomes a paste; then properly treat the wounds with the other treatment until they are healed.
But if a bone fracture occurs with the wound and it is small, then remove it with tweezers.
And I will describe the cure for fractures of the head in what follows.
Of wounds on the neck:
But if a wound occurs on the neck, then it does not differ in treatment from a simple wound on the head.
But if the neck's nerve or artery is cut, then if it is a nerve, it should not be treated with anything that causes violent contraction, as well as aconite and arnica which are like vitriol and its likes because they harm nerves and cause constriction. And do not apply to the wound anything that causes any heat, for the substance of nerves is sensitive to heat and their continuity is through the brain, which is the source of all members.
And if it is treated with mild medicines, as well as being washed with tepid water, any poultice infused in rose oil or other oils, and oozing when washed with tepid water and the other stones according to this manner, and moist bandages.
But if the wound is large, then administer stitches, or tie together its lips, and properly treat it with powder until it is healed.
But if the wound is deep or there is pus in it, then pierce it in its most depressed part.
But if the wound has cut an artery and blood flows from it, then stop or dry it, or ligature it, or cauterize it if necessity compels you to do so.
But if the windpipe or all of it is cut and the neck' veins are saved, then close the lips of the wound with stitches over the windpipe and do not touch it; release that and return it to its natural shape, and properly bind it with a decent bandage, and let it be bound by a tight bandage for several days; then treat it with ointments in which there is contraction and excitement until it is healed.
But if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then pierce it, and if there are fragments of bone in it, extract them all that you can; and what you cannot extract, let it be so that the wound suppurates, and the separation of it is relieved.
And if the wound is recent, then apply powder to it which I have described. But if a fistula has formed in the wound, then treat it with what its memory will bring to you later in this chapter.
If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and you see its depth, then consider, for if the patient is pale, know that the wound is deadly.
And if there is no depth to it and the wound is recent with its blood, then apply to it in the first hour powder, and do not bind it tightly so that the blood is not retained in its depth and returning to the heart and the patient does not faint, but apply an attractive ointment to it, and loose it twice a day.
And if the ointment is not at hand, then you should stop the orifice of the plague with a piece of wool so that it sucks out what comes from the humidity; and make the patient sleep on his side so that what is inside him can flow out.
But if three or more days have passed since the plague and the patient has not experienced spasms, nor a bad heart tremor, nor a stricture of the throat, and you see his other dispositions are good, then know that he is saved from the plague; then heal him with leeches and other remedies until he is healed.
But if his healing is delayed and the wound remains open for a long time, then know that a fistula has formed; therefore, heal it according to its nature.
And if the plague is a cut from a spear or dagger and is superficial on the foot or leg, then heal it with what is preceded by sewing, if it is large, or with powder, if it is small.
But if there has already been damage to the bone and pieces of it are sticking out, then you should twist the wound and cut to extract those pieces, if they are separated. But if they are not separated, then let them remain inside until the wound is healed, for their extraction is painful.
And for other plagues that occur in other limbs, the cure is the same as what we have already said.
Of plagues of the belly:
The disorder that occurs in the belly is either great, or small, or medium-sized.
And a small disruption is made difficult in another way, and you see that their reduction is more difficult if you do not stop the intrusion of them into their place immediately, for it opens and swells so that its interior is made difficult.
And therefore the best disruption is medium-sized, for in that one the reduction of the intestine is not difficult, just as it is difficult in the two species mentioned before.
And know that there are four ways of sewing the belly, but two sutures are common to all other sutures of the body.
And two other sutures are specific to the others plagues, but nonetheless they are more specific in the sewing of the belly.
I will return to you each one with exposure and explanation.
Therefore I say that when the plague is small and there has been some cause of the intestine through it, and it is difficult to reduce it, then it is in one of two ways: either by smallness of the disruption as we have said, or when the intestine is received inflammation due to the chill of the air.
And therefore when that is so, you should warm it in such a way that you immerse a sponge or damp cloth in water with only teasel, or you gather in squinant water, and cyperum, and spic, and embrocate with that the intestine until the inflammation is resolved.
And sometimes it does this in the thing in which there has been constriction, and it is better than water alone in resolving inflammation.
And therefore when you see the inflammation is resolved, then you should moisten the intestine with water in which there is added mallows and alder, for by that the interior of it is eased with little cause.
But if its interior is not eased by this cure, then split the disruption a little with an instrument by which the hemorrhoids are split.
And the first cure is better when it is not cut, and there is no need to dry it up and starve it.
Of the instrument, know its shape:
One part of it is bent acute, and the other part not acute, and the end be subtle, and its subtlety not be like a spatula, but rather be blunt a little.
And therefore when the plague is enlarged and comes out of the intestine, then you should see that its reduction is according to its natural shape, in its proper place, if possible, for that is better.
But when the disruption is wide and it is in the lower part of the belly, then you should have the patient lie on his back, and place his legs above his head; and if it is in the higher part of the belly, then you should place his head and feet below.
And similarly if the disruption is in one of the two parts of the belly, then pay your attention and consideration to that always so that the part in which there is the plague is higher than the other.
And thus you should manage this in great plagues and in medium-sized plagues.
And in small plagues, do what is prepared for you, and let the minister be between your fingers, holding the plague all around with his hand and uncovering it to see that there is no sewing any cause whatsoever.
And this is the common way of sewing: one where you take the needle, or count of needles according to the amount of the amplitude of the plague; and let go of the end of the disruption of the finger, and tighten the needle one, and then you do not put thread in the two ends of the string, with two ends of the thread that is below the fingers, within the fingers, so that you make the needle penetrate from that part; and you have added the two ends of the thread and the two ends of the thread, and so you have made four turns.
And then tighten with double thread around the needle, and sometimes from two parts together, and then bring the two lips and the plague by gathering decently; and let go of the thickness of the finger and take another needle in that, and then tie it with a thread as it was with the first needle; and do not cease doing this if there is a need for needles until all the contraction of the plague is completed.
And let the needles be between thinness and subtlety, for thin needles penetrate quickly into the flesh; and thick ones are of difficult intrusion into the flesh, and therefore let them be thinner in subtlety and thickness.
And let the needle not be pushed into two ends of the wound near each other, so that the flesh is not quickly split and the plague opens before its consolidation.
And they are not prolonged in sewing so that the plague is not prohibited from consolidation.
And then insert the ends of the needles so that they do not tickle the patient when he wakes from his sleep; and you shall place over the sutures expanded flours from all sides, which have the ends of the needles; and let go of them when you know that the plague is consolidated.
And these species of sewing with needles in this manner is more convenient in small plagues, for they have in their sewing one needle or two or around them.
But the second sewing is common: and it is that you manage with sewing the four ends, of the wound and two ends of the thread, in one go, with a needle in which there is thread wrapped around in both thinness and thickness.
And then when you have the needle penetrated these four ends, reduce the needle of that part from which it started, so that the thread drawn back goes through the most superficial part of the plague, so that the sewing is according to sewing with cloth in which the clothes are tight.
And place between each stitch an amount equal to the thickness of the little finger.
This stitch is known to men.
And with this stitch I healed the wound of a man in his belly who had been stabbed with a knife, and it was an injury of a palm's width, and it had exited the intestines about two palms from the navel and it was a disruption in the middle of the body; and then I healed him after the intestine had been punctured through the wound for twenty-four hours.
And the wound was healed in about fifteen days, and he was cured, and he is doing well now, and his condition has returned to normal.
And the other doctors had judged that he would not be healed; and by a miracle I healed him without ointment, for it was in a place where ointments were not effective or any medicine, but I placed cotton wool on the wound two times a day and washed it frequently with honey water until it was healed.
But I will describe two kinds of stitches according to the narration of the Lord.
And you should start with the stitch of the cord, and insert the needle from the outside inwards.
And then the needle penetrates through the cord and the surrounding tissues according to its direction and length throughout the whole body, and leaves the end of the thread in which you inserted the needle; and make the needle penetrate from the inside out on the other end of the body into the other end of the thread.
And when you have made that one penetrate, then you make the other one penetrate in that end of the body from the inside out; and leave the end of the thread on this side, and make the needle penetrate into the other end from the outside in.
And make it penetrate with that penetration with which you make the other one penetrate in the end of the body which is inside, so that everything penetrates.
And then start from this side of the body and sew that with the end which is of the cord on the other side, and pull the needle out of the cord which has been penetrated, and then return it into that cord and sew the end of the thread which is on the other side of the body with that end of the body; and pull that one out of the cord which belongs to him.
And do that once and again, and do that another time within so that you sew everything which is outside according to that example.
And the sum of this method of sewing is that you sew with a stitch of skin in which the skin is sewn, so that you sew the cord one time from the end of the thread, and then you sew the other end so that it is completed.
But the second special stitch which I describe is called Gualia, and it is made of silk thread and rewoven through him, so that you sew it according to its shape with which some doctors sew it, in such a way that they unite each part to its corresponding part according to nature; and they apply one end of him to the other end of the body, and that is done according to how I have taught you.
Take the needle and put it in the end of the body towards you from the outside, and make it penetrate to the inside in that sole, and leave two ends of the thread; and then turn the needle and make it penetrate from the inside out into two ends of the thread.
And then turn those ones, and make the others penetrate from the inside out into two ends of the body which are on the contrary side.
And this method of sewing is better than common stitching, and it is the stitch which I previously described in memory.
This is the thread of Gualia.
And some say that the stitch of the belly is straightened with two needles, so you put in these one by one a thread, and start with the penetration of the needle from what is facing you, and make it penetrate into the other side according to the sewing of those who sew bodies together mouth to mouth.
And know that when there is a disruption in the middle of the belly, then its sewing is more difficult than in other places of the belly.
But the medication of wound is judgment of the other wounds.
The cause is that when you see the wound fresh with its blood in front of the air which alters it, and reduce the intestine and sew it and adjust it decently, then put on it powder which makes flesh.

But if you do not have the medicines at your presence, then put it on immediately, because as soon as it starts to boil, change it two times a day, and permute it two times a day, just as I have taught you, until it is healed, for you do not need other medicine in various conditions when the wounds are simple.
But if you fear that the wound will spread to the principal members, then take a woolen thread and submerge it in oil of excellent quality, or in rose oil, and put it on the circumference of the places which are between the ankles and below the heels.
And if you feel pain or putrefaction in your intestines, especially when it happens several times, then scorch that with black styptic wine, and especially if the putrefaction is caused by the intestine and has made an opening penetrating into its cavity.
And know that which is of the gross intestine is a more difficult cure than that which is in the subtle intestines.
And it is of difficult cure because the intestine which is called "gegunu" does not receive healing of wound which pierces in him from all; and that is because of the great multitude of veins which are in him and because of his magnitude which is in those, and because of the subtlety of his body and because of its proximity to the nature of nerves.
But if what proceeds from the wound is the thread, and you obtain it fresh, then reduce it according to your instruction with which you reduce the intestines evenly.
But if it has passed through him and is already black or green, then tie that with a thread over the place which is blackened in him, so that there comes flux of blood, for in the thread there are veins and arteries.
And then insert that which is another that, and put two ends of the thread hanging from the end below the wound out of him, so that over you be elevated the attraction of him because of the lowering of the thread and the emission of the pus of the wound.
Memory of the wounds when they happen in the intestine.

And it is feared for its wickedness, for when it goes in the body and is elevated to the head and has come to the throat, then it breaks out and penetrates and destroys the throat, and that therefrom many times.
And therefore when you want to heal and extract it, then it is not done unless through its walking and appearance to the feeling, and then when you press what is above it and what is below it with strong binding and contraction, and then dry over it and extract it.

But if you want that to come to the head near the throat, then bind strongly over the forehead and press over it and extract it; and when the patient uses cleansing of his body with evacuating medicines and abstains from food generating putrefaction, then he guards himself from bad and putrid humors.

And he had seen before that in my own body according to that way, but he had seen move which bear pain being transferred from limb to limb. But I did not see it with the arms like in the woman.

And it is necessary that it does not appear according to this back-cure in those who are delicate and of body with humors mixed with veins.

Of extraction of arrows.
Arrows are diversified according to spices, and according to the places of the body in which they are placed, for their diversity is that some have great points, and small, and concave, and hollow, and from them that have three angles, and those to which there are tongues; and from those to which there are astels.
And the signs of the soul are when an arrow pierces him, and penetrates the bone, and is situated in the sipho which is above the brain, because it happens through it violently, and scotomata, and vertigo, and burning in the eyes, and inflammation and heat of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of the mind and vomiting of bile, and the speech is very feeble and destroyed, and there comes out of the site of the wound a white humidity similar to pus, and his eyes are like water.
And therefore if you see these signs, then you abstain from the cure and the extraction of the arrow, unless it is exposed.
But the signs of the arrow when it pierces the heart are that it is near the left nipple, and one feels that it has been struck with a hard object, and it is not a superficial wound; and soon the movement of the arrow is similar to the movement of the pulse, and black blood flows from the wound, and there is coldness in the extremities, and a hissing sound, and syncope; and therefore know that death is descending with certainty.
And the signs when the arrow has wounded the lungs are foaming blood coming out of the wound, and the vessels near the neck are swollen, and the color of the patient changes, and he breathes heavily, and demands frequent breathing.
And if the arrow pierces the membrane which is in the chest, then the pain is near the small ribs, and there is made a great wound with violent pain and with sighing, and not all the members of the muscles are affected.
And if the arrow pierces the stomach, then soon you will see from the wound some undigested food.
And if the arrow pierces the abdomen and is stuck in it, you will see some slit in the wound, or the membrane, or intestine which is torn, and there is no hope for cure by extracting the arrow.
And if the arrow pierces the bladder and urine flows out of it, and some cause processes outside of it to the exit, and there is strong pain on the patient, then know that it is deadly.
But the other members, such as the face, neck, collarbone, shoulders, vertebrae of the back, sternum, thigh, and their likes of the members, are saved according to the most serious dispositions when the arrow does not hit a vein or artery, and is not a venomous arrow.

The cause of which is that in a man who has an arrow in the tear duct of his eye socket in the root of his nose, if I extract that from him from the other side, below the gray matter of his brain, he will be healed and no harm will come to his eye.

Thus begins the treatment of the third part: of restoration. This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine; and it is the restoration of fracture and accidental dislocation in the bones.
Oh son, know that the foolish doctors and the common people and those who for any length of time did not read the books of the Ancients nor understood a letter of them.
And for this cause it has happened that this manner of the scientists in our land is neglected; and I have not practiced it at any time on account of all; and I have not employed what I learned, except through length of reading the books of the Ancients and study about their understanding, so as to extract the science from them.
And I have added experience and study in the length of my life.

Diversity of fracture in itself. There is a sign for fracture of the bone. And by this is a fracture of the bone known: it is its crookedness and appearance to the sense, and feel of it when you press on it with your hand.
And therefore when there is no crookedness apparent in the place nor anything done because of your touching when you move the bone and the patient feels no great pain then there is not here a fracture.
It is possible that there be crookedness or slight fissure, then it does not behoove you to press on it with your hand and with compression altogether; rather pause over it medicines of which come recollection properly to the place; and let it be bound tightly with a subtle ligature.
And know that the place when it is arched and not split in two or anything else that does not happen in it satiation, as is rememered all separated from its kind, then it behooves you to begin from your hour at rectification of it lest what happens in it be cautery.
And if what happens in it is cautery, then let it be that for some days until the cautery ceases; and let the wound heal according to whatever way you can of elevation and painlessness.
And know that restoration of it and piercing of it is more difficult than of the bone in which occurs satiation.
